### Configure Workshop Setup with postStartCommand

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/blog/posts/2025-05-19-quarto-codespaces/index.llms

Configures a container to automatically install Python dependencies or run initialization scripts upon startup.

```json
{
  "name": "My Workshop Setup",
  "image": "ghcr.io/mcanouil/quarto-codespaces:latest",
  "remoteUser": "vscode",
  "postStartCommand": "uv venv && source .venv/bin/activate && uv pip install -r requirements.txt"
}
```

```json
{
  "name": "My Workshop Setup",
  "image": "ghcr.io/mcanouil/quarto-codespaces:latest",
  "remoteUser": "vscode",
  "postStartCommand": "bash ./init-env.sh --what all --force" // <1>
}
```

### quarto use

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/cli/use.llms

Automate document or project setup tasks. This is the main command with subcommands for specific setup actions.

```APIDOC
## quarto use

### Description
Automate document or project setup tasks.

### Method
CLI Command

### Endpoint
quarto use <type:string> [target:string]

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
- **type** (string) - Required - The type of setup task to perform (e.g., template, binder, brand).
- **target** (string) - Optional - The target for the setup task, such as a template name or repository.

#### Query Parameters
None

#### Request Body
None

### Options
#### Flags
- **--no-prompt** - Do not prompt to confirm actions

### Commands
#### template
Use a Quarto template for this directory or project.

#### binder
Configure the current project with Binder support.

#### brand
Use a brand for this project.
```

#| context: setup
import seaborn as sns
penguins = sns.load_dataset("penguins")

### Request for Reproducible Example

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/triaging/index.llms

This template guides users on how to provide a small, self-contained, reproducible example for their issue. It emphasizes the importance of making it easy for developers to recreate the problem and offers specific instructions for Quarto documents and Git repositories.

```markdown
Could you share a **small self-contained "working" (reproducible)** example to work with, _i.e._, a complete Quarto document or a Git repository? The goal is to make it as easy as possible for us to recreate your problem so that we can fix it: please help us help you! Thanks.

---

You can share a **self-contained "working" (reproducible)** Quarto document using the following syntax, _i.e._, using more backticks than you have in your document (usually four ` ```` `).
See <https://quarto.org/bug-reports.html#small-is-beautiful-aim-for-a-single-document-with-10-lines>.

If you have multiple files (and if it is **absolutely required** to have multiple files), please share as a Git repository.

<table>
<tr><th>R</th><th>Python</th></tr>
<tr><td>

`````md
````qmd
---
title: "Reproducible Quarto Document"
format: html
engine: knitr
---

This is a reproducible Quarto document.

{{< lipsum 1 >}}

```{r}
x <- c(1, 2, 3, 4, 5)
y <- c(1, 4, 9, 16, 25)

plot(x, y)
```

![An image]({{< placeholder 600 400 >}}){#fig-placeholder}

{{< lipsum 1 >}}

The end after @fig-placeholder.
````
`````

</td><td>

`````md
````qmd
---
title: "Reproducible Quarto Document"
format: html
engine: jupyter
---

This is a reproducible Quarto document.

{{< lipsum 1 >}}

```{python}
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

x = [1, 2, 3, 4, 5]
y = [1, 4, 9, 16, 25]

plt.plot(x, y)
plt.show()
```

![An image]({{< placeholder 600 400 >}}){#fig-placeholder}

{{< lipsum 1 >}}

The end after @fig-placeholder.
````
`````

</td></tr>
</table>

Additionally and if not already given, please share the output of `quarto check` within a code block (*i.e.*, using three backticks ` ```txt `), see <https://quarto.org/bug-reports.html#check>.
``````
```

### Configure GitHub Action for Jupyter with venv

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/publishing/github-pages.llms

A complete workflow example that sets up Python, installs dependencies from requirements.txt, and publishes to GitHub Pages.

```yaml
on:
  workflow_dispatch:
  push:
    branches: main

name: Quarto Publish

jobs:
  build-deploy:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    permissions:
      contents: write
    steps:
      - name: Check out repository
        uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - name: Set up Quarto
        uses: quarto-dev/quarto-actions/setup@v2

      - name: Install Python and Dependencies
        uses: actions/setup-python@v5
        with:
          python-version: '3.10'
          cache: 'pip'
      - run: pip install jupyter
      - run: pip install -r requirements.txt

      - name: Render and Publish
        uses: quarto-dev/quarto-actions/publish@v2
        with:
          target: gh-pages
        env:
          GITHUB_TOKEN: ${{ secrets.GITHUB_TOKEN }}
```

### GET /list

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/cli/list.llms

Lists installed extensions or global dependencies based on the provided type argument.

```APIDOC
## GET list

### Description
Lists an extension or global dependency.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
quarto list <type>

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
- **type** (string) - Required - The category to list (e.g., 'extensions', 'tools')

#### Query Parameters
- **--log** (string) - Optional - Path to log file
- **--log-level** (string) - Optional - Log level (debug, info, warning, error, critical)
- **--log-format** (string) - Optional - Log format (plain, json-stream)
- **--quiet** (boolean) - Optional - Suppress console output
- **--profile** (string) - Optional - Active project profile(s)

### Request Example
quarto list extensions

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **output** (string) - A list of installed items corresponding to the requested type.
```

### Publish to Netlify with Auth Token and _publish.yml

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/publishing/ci.llms

This example shows how to publish to Netlify using an authentication token and a `_publish.yml` file. Ensure the NETLIFY_AUTH_TOKEN environment variable is set.

```bash
# credentials from https://app.netlify.com/user/applications
export NETLIFY_AUTH_TOKEN="45fd6ae56c"

# publish to the netlify site id provided within _publish.yml
quarto publish netlify
```

### Complete website draft configuration

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/websites/website-drafts.llms

```yaml
project:
  type: website

website:
  title: "Cool Website."
  navbar:
    left:
      - stuff/item1.qmd
      - stuff/item2.qmd
  drafts:                   # <1>
    - stuff/item2.qmd       # <1>
  draft-mode: unlinked      # <2>
```

### Example _extension.yml for Auto-Detection

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/advanced/typst/typst-gather.llms

Configure your extension's Typst files in `_extension.yml`. These files will be scanned for package imports.

```yaml
contributes:
  formats:
    typst:
      template: template.typ
      template-partials:
        - typst-template.typ
        - typst-show.typ
```

### Quarto Install Command

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/cli/install.llms

The 'quarto install' command is used to install global dependencies required by Quarto. You can specify the target dependency or run it without arguments to choose interactively.

```APIDOC
## QUARTO INSTALL

### Description
Installs a global dependency (TinyTeX, Chromium, Chrome Headless Shell, VeraPDF).

### Method
CLI Command

### Endpoint
`quarto install [target...]`

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
- **target** (string) - Optional - The specific dependency to install (e.g., `tinytex`, `chrome-headless-shell`, `chromium`). If not provided, the user will be prompted to choose.

#### Query Parameters
None

#### Request Body
None

### Options
- **-h, --help** - Show this help message.
- **--no-prompt** - Do not prompt to confirm actions.
- **--update-path** - Update system path when a tool is installed.
- **--log** (string) - Path to log file.
- **--log-level** (string) - Log level (debug, info, warning, error, critical).
- **--log-format** (string) - Log format (plain, json-stream).
- **--quiet** - Suppress console output.
- **--profile** (string) - Active project profile(s).

### Commands
- **help** - Show this help or the help of a sub-command.

### Examples

#### Install TinyTeX
```bash
quarto install tinytex
```

#### Install Chrome Headless Shell
```bash
quarto install chrome-headless-shell
```

#### Install Chromium (legacy)
```bash
quarto install chromium
```

#### Choose tool to install interactively
```bash
quarto install
```
```

--------------------------------

### Install Extension from GitHub

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/cli/add.llms

Install a Quarto extension directly from a GitHub repository. Replace <gh-org>/<gh-repo> with the organization and repository name.

```bash
quarto add <gh-org>/<gh-repo>
```

### Basic Slide Structure with Headings

```markdown

title: "Habits"
author: "John Doe"
format: pptx
---

## Getting up

- Turn off alarm
- Get out of bed

## Going to sleep

- Get in bed
- Count sheep

```

Tool         Status            Installed     Latest
chromium     Not installed     ---           869685
tinytex      Up to date        v2022.10      v2022.10

```bash
quarto update tinytex
```

```bash
quarto uninstall tinytex
```

--------------------------------

### Quarto Tarball Installation on Linux

Source: https://quarto.org/llms.txt

This command installs Quarto from a tarball on Linux. It involves downloading, extracting, and adding the binary to the system's PATH. Ensure you have `wget` and `tar` installed.

```bash
wget https://github.com/quarto-dev/quarto-cli/releases/download/v1.4.310/quarto-1.4.310-linux-amd64.tar.gz
tar -xzf quarto-1.4.310-linux-amd64.tar.gz
sudo mv quarto-1.4.310/bin/quarto /usr/local/bin/
sudo rm -rf quarto-1.4.310 quarto-1.4.310-linux-amd64.tar.gz
```

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/publishing/rstudio-connect.llms

Example of environment variables and the `quarto publish` command to deploy content to Posit Connect when a `_publish.yml` file is present. Ensure `CONNECT_SERVER` and `CONNECT_API_KEY` are set.

```bash
export CONNECT_SERVER=https://connect.example.com/
export CONNECT_API_KEY=7C0947A852D8
quarto publish connect
```

### Create a Quarto Computations Document

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/get-started/computations/text-editor.llms

Initial structure for a .qmd file including NumPy, Matplotlib, and Plotly examples.

```markdown
---
title: Quarto Computations
jupyter: python3
---

## NumPy

```{python}
import numpy as np
a = np.arange(15).reshape(3, 5)
a
```

## Matplotlib

```{python}
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

fig = plt.figure()
x = np.arange(10)
y = 2.5 * np.sin(x / 20 * np.pi)
yerr = np.linspace(0.05, 0.2, 10)

plt.errorbar(x, y + 3, yerr=yerr, label='both limits (default)')
plt.errorbar(x, y + 2, yerr=yerr, uplims=True, label='uplims=True')
plt.errorbar(x, y + 1, yerr=yerr, uplims=True, lolims=True,
             label='uplims=True, lolims=True')

upperlimits = [True, False] * 5
lowerlimits = [False, True] * 5
plt.errorbar(x, y, yerr=yerr, uplims=upperlimits, lolims=lowerlimits,
             label='subsets of uplims and lolims')

plt.legend(loc='lower right')
plt.show(fig)
```

## Plotly

```{python}
import plotly.express as px
import plotly.io as pio
gapminder = px.data.gapminder()
gapminder2007 = gapminder.query("year == 2007")
fig = px.scatter(gapminder2007, 
                 x="gdpPercap", y="lifeExp", color="continent", 
                 size="pop", size_max=60,
                 hover_name="country")
fig.show()
```
```

### FizzBuzz Implementation Examples

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/output-formats/html-basics.llms

Example functions demonstrating FizzBuzz logic across different programming languages.

```r
fizz_buzz <- function(fbnums = 1:50) {
  output <- dplyr::case_when(
    fbnums %% 15 == 0 ~ "FizzBuzz",
    fbnums %% 3 == 0 ~ "Fizz",
    fbnums %% 5 == 0 ~ "Buzz",
    TRUE ~ as.character(fbnums)
  )
  print(output)
}
```

```python
def fizz_buzz(num):
  if num % 15 == 0:
    print("FizzBuzz")
  elif num % 5 == 0:
    print("Buzz")
  elif num % 3 == 0:
    print("Fizz")
  else:
    print(num)
```

```java
public class FizzBuzz
{
  public static void fizzBuzz(int num)
  {
    if (num % 15 == 0) {
      System.out.println("FizzBuzz");
    } else if (num % 5 == 0) {
      System.out.println("Buzz");
    } else if (num % 3 == 0) {
      System.out.println("Fizz");
    } else {
      System.out.println(num);
    }
  }
}
```

```julia
function FizzBuzz(num)
  if num % 15 == 0
    println("FizzBuzz")
  elseif num % 5 == 0
    println("Buzz")
  elseif num % 3 == 0
    println("Fizz")
  else
    println(num)
  end
end
```

### Custom Node Example: Callout

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/advanced/quarto-ast.llms

Example of modifying a Callout AST node in a Lua filter.

```APIDOC
## Lua Filter Example: Modifying Callout Type

### Description
This Lua filter demonstrates how to target and modify a `Callout` AST node. It forces every callout to be of type "caution".

### Method
N/A (Filter execution)

### Endpoint
N/A (Filter execution)

### Parameters
N/A

### Request Example
N/A

### Response
N/A (AST modification)

### Code Example
```lua
function Callout(callout)
  -- do something with the callout
  callout.type = "caution"

  -- note that custom AST nodes are passed by reference. You can
  -- return the value if you choose, but you do not need to.
end
```
```

### Example typst-gather.toml Configuration

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/advanced/typst/typst-gather.llms

This TOML file allows detailed configuration of package gathering, including root directory, destination, and files to discover.

```toml
# typst-gather configuration
# Run: quarto call typst-gather

rootdir = "_extensions/myformat"
destination = "typst/packages"

discover = ["typst-template.typ", "typst-show.typ"]

# Preview packages are auto-discovered from imports.
# Uncomment to pin specific versions:
# [preview]
# marginalia = "0.3.1"
# cetz = "0.4.1"

# Local packages (@local namespace) must be configured manually.
# [local]
# my-pkg = "/path/to/my-pkg"
```

### Example Quarto Document for Hugo

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/output-formats/hugo.llms

This is an example `index.qmd` file for a Hugo page bundle. It includes front matter, specifies the `hugo-md` format, and contains a Python code chunk for generating a plot.

```markdown
---
title: Hello, Quarto
date: "2012-04-06"
categories: 
  - Matplotlib
  - Coordinates
format: hugo-md
jupyter: python3
---

## Polar Axis

For a demonstration of a line plot on a polar axis, see @fig-polar.

```{python}
#| label: fig-polar
#| fig-cap: "A line plot on a polar axis"

import numpy as np
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

r = np.arange(0, 2, 0.01)
theta = 2 * np.pi * r
fig, ax = plt.subplots(subplot_kw={'projection': 'polar'})
ax.plot(theta, r)
ax.set_rticks([0.5, 1, 1.5, 2])
ax.grid(True)
plt.show()
```
```

### Preview Jupyter Notebook with Quarto

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/computations/julia.llms

This command starts a live preview of a Jupyter notebook. The preview updates automatically when the notebook is saved.

```bash
quarto preview document.ipynb
```

--------------------------------

### Render with Command-Line Parameters

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/computations/parameters.llms

Render a Quarto document with specific parameter values using the `-P` flag on the command line. This applies to both .ipynb and .qmd files.

```bash
quarto render document.ipynb -P alpha:0.2 -P ratio:0.3
```

### Install Shiny and Shinywidgets Packages

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/dashboards/interactivity/shiny-python/running.llms

Install or upgrade the latest versions of the 'shiny' and 'shinywidgets' packages. Ensure you have version 0.9.0 or higher for Shiny and 0.3.1 or higher for shinywidgets.

```bash
pip install --upgrade shiny shinywidgets
```

### Python Reproducible Quarto Document Example

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/triaging/index.llms

An example of a minimal, reproducible Quarto document using Python as the engine. It includes YAML front matter, basic markdown content, a Python code chunk for plotting, and an image placeholder.

```qmd
---
title: "Reproducible Quarto Document"
format: html
engine: jupyter
---

This is a reproducible Quarto document.

{{< lipsum 1 >}}

```{python}
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

x = [1, 2, 3, 4, 5]
y = [1, 4, 9, 16, 25]

plt.plot(x, y)
plt.show()
```

![An image]({{< placeholder 600 400 >}}){#fig-placeholder}

{{< lipsum 1 >}}

The end after @fig-placeholder.
```

--------------------------------

### Example Quarto SCSS Theme File

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/output-formats/html-themes-more.llms

A basic Quarto theme file demonstrating the structure with functions, defaults, and rules. Ensure at least one region decorator is present for validity.

```css
/*-- scss:functions --*/
@function colorToRGB ($color) {
  @return "rgb(" + red($color) + ", " + green($color) + ", " + blue($color)+ ")";
}

/*-- scss:defaults --*/
$h2-font-size:          1.6rem !default;
$headings-font-weight:  500 !default;

/*-- scss:rules --*/
h1, h2, h3, h4, h5, h6 {
  text-shadow: -1px -1px 0 rgba(0, 0, 0, .3);
}
```

### CLI Command: quarto create

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/cli/create.llms

Initializes a new Quarto project or extension with optional editor integration and logging configurations.

```APIDOC
## CLI COMMAND: quarto create

### Description
Create a Quarto project or extension.

### Method
CLI Command

### Endpoint
quarto create [type] [commands...]

### Parameters
#### Options
- **-h, --help** - Optional - Show this help.
- **--open** (string) - Optional - Open new artifact in this editor (positron, vscode, rstudio).
- **--no-open** - Optional - Do not open in an editor.
- **--no-prompt** - Optional - Do not prompt to confirm actions.
- **--log** - Optional - Path to log file.
- **--log-level** - Optional - Log level (debug, info, warning, error, critical).
- **--log-format** - Optional - Log format (plain, json-stream).
- **--quiet** - Optional - Suppress console output.
- **--profile** - Optional - Active project profile(s).
```

--------------------------------

### Configure GitHub Action for Knitr with renv

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/publishing/github-pages.llms

A complete workflow example that sets up R, restores dependencies from renv.lock, and publishes to GitHub Pages.

```yaml
on:
  workflow_dispatch:
  push:
    branches: main

name: Quarto Publish

jobs:
  build-deploy:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    permissions:
      contents: write
    steps:
      - name: Check out repository
        uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - name: Set up Quarto
        uses: quarto-dev/quarto-actions/setup@v2

      - name: Install R
        uses: r-lib/actions/setup-r@v2
        with:
          r-version: '4.2.0'

      - name: Install R Dependencies
        uses: r-lib/actions/setup-renv@v2
        with:
          cache-version: 1

      - name: Render and Publish
        uses: quarto-dev/quarto-actions/publish@v2
        with:
          target: gh-pages
        env:
          GITHUB_TOKEN: ${{ secrets.GITHUB_TOKEN }}
```

### Check R Installation with knitr

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/troubleshooting/index.llms

Run this R code within a .qmd file to inspect the R installation Quarto is using. It helps diagnose issues if Quarto is finding an incorrect R version. The `sessioninfo` package provides more readable output and can write results to a file for comparison.

```r
sessionInfo()
Sys.getenv()
.libPaths()

# If the sessioninfo package is available, 
# it provides output that is easier to read,
# and can write its results to a file
sessioninfo:::session_info(to_file = "quarto-session-info-output.txt")
```

```r
sessioninfo:::session_diff(new = "quarto-session-info-output.txt")
```

### Full Scholarly Front Matter Example

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/authoring/front-matter.llms

This YAML header includes examples of top-level keys for scholarly articles, such as title, date, author details, abstract, keywords, license, copyright, citation, and funding.

```yaml
---
title: "Toward a Unified Theory of High-Energy Metaphysics: Silly String Theory"
date: 2008-02-29
author:
  - name: Josiah Carberry
    id: jc
    orcid: 0000-0002-1825-0097
    email: josiah@psychoceramics.org
    affiliation: 
      - name: Brown University
        city: Providence
        state: RI
        url: www.brown.edu
abstract: > 
  The characteristic theme of the works of Stone is 
  the bridge between culture and society. ...
keywords:
  - Metaphysics
  - String Theory
license: "CC BY"
copyright: 
  holder: Josiah Carberry
  year: 2008
citation: 
  container-title: Journal of Psychoceramics
  volume: 1
  issue: 1
  doi: 10.5555/12345678
funding: "The author received no specific funding for this work."
---

```

--------------------------------

### GitHub Action: Jupyter with venv for Quarto Publish

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/publishing/netlify.llms

Use this GitHub Action to set up Python, install Jupyter and project dependencies, and publish Quarto content to Netlify. Ensure `requirements.txt` is present in your repository.

```yaml
on:
  workflow_dispatch:
  push:
    branches: main

name: Quarto Publish

jobs:
  build-deploy:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Check out repository
        uses: actions/checkout@v4 

      - name: Set up Quarto
        uses: quarto-dev/quarto-actions/setup@v2
        
      - name: Install Python and Dependencies
        uses: actions/setup-python@v5
        with:
          python-version: '3.10'
          cache: 'pip'
      - run: pip install jupyter
      - run: pip install -r requirements.txt
      
      - name: Render and Publish 
        uses: quarto-dev/quarto-actions/publish@v2
        with:
          target: netlify
          NETLIFY_AUTH_TOKEN: ${{ secrets.NETLIFY_AUTH_TOKEN }}
```

### Example of a built-in theme source

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/presentations/revealjs/themes.llms

The serif theme demonstrates how to define variables with !default and apply specific CSS rules.

```default
/*-- scss:defaults --*/

// fonts
$font-family-sans-serif: "Palatino Linotype", "Book Antiqua", Palatino,
  FreeSerif, serif !default;

// colors
$body-bg: #f0f1eb !default;
$body-color: #000 !default;
$link-color: #51483d !default;
$selection-bg: #26351c !default;

// headings
$presentation-heading-font: "Palatino Linotype", "Book Antiqua", Palatino,
  FreeSerif, serif !default;
$presentation-heading-color: #383d3d !default;

/*-- scss:rules --*/

.reveal a {
  line-height: 1.3em;
}
```

--------------------------------

### Publish Quarto Project with Python and venv

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/publishing/quarto-pub.llms

Use this action to set up Python, install project dependencies from requirements.txt, and publish your Quarto project. Ensure QUARTO_PUB_AUTH_TOKEN is set in your GitHub secrets.

```yaml
on:
  workflow_dispatch:
  push:
    branches: main

name: Quarto Publish

jobs:
  build-deploy:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Check out repository
        uses: actions/checkout@v4 

      - name: Set up Quarto
        uses: quarto-dev/quarto-actions/setup@v2
        
      - name: Install Python and Dependencies
        uses: actions/setup-python@v5
        with:
          python-version: '3.10'
          cache: 'pip'
      - run: pip install jupyter
      - run: pip install -r requirements.txt
      
      - name: Render and Publish 
        uses: quarto-dev/quarto-actions/publish@v2
        with:
          target: quarto-pub
          QUARTO_PUB_AUTH_TOKEN: ${{ secrets.QUARTO_PUB_AUTH_TOKEN }}
```

### CLI Commands for TeX Management

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/output-formats/pdf-engine.llms

Commands to install, update, list, and uninstall the TinyTeX distribution used by Quarto.

```APIDOC
## CLI Commands

### Description
Commands to manage the TinyTeX installation environment.

### Commands
- `quarto install tinytex`: Installs TinyTeX.
- `quarto install tinytex --update-path`: Installs TinyTeX and adds it to the system PATH.
- `quarto list tools`: Lists installed tools and versions.
- `quarto update tinytex`: Updates TinyTeX to the latest version.
- `quarto uninstall tinytex`: Removes the TinyTeX installation.
```

### Include Content in Quarto HTML Format

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/output-formats/html-basics.llms

  html:
    include-in-header:
      - text: |
          <script src="https://examples.org/demo.js"></script>
      - file: analytics.html
      - comments.html
    include-before-body: header.html
```

### Define Notebook in Markdown

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/tools/jupyter-lab.llms

Example of a .qmd file structure including YAML front matter and an embedded Python code chunk.

```markdown
---
title: "Matplotlib Demo"
author: "Norah Smith"
date: "5/22/2021"
format: 
  html:
    code-fold: true
jupyter: python3
---

## Polar Axis

For a demonstration of a line plot on a polar axis, see @fig-polar.

```{python}
#| label: fig-polar
#| fig-cap: "A line plot on a polar axis"

import numpy as np
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

r = np.arange(0, 2, 0.01)
theta = 2 * np.pi * r
fig, ax = plt.subplots(subplot_kw={'projection': 'polar'})
ax.plot(theta, r)
ax.set_rticks([0.5, 1, 1.5, 2])
ax.grid(True)
plt.show()
```
```

### Create custom layout Shiny document

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/interactive/shiny/index.llms

A full-page application example using custom layout panels and reactive clustering.

```markdown
---
title: "Iris K-Means Clustering"
format: 
  html:
    page-layout: custom
server: shiny
---

```{r}
#| panel: sidebar
vars <- setdiff(names(iris), "Species")
selectInput('xcol', 'X Variable', vars)
selectInput('ycol', 'Y Variable', vars, selected = vars[[2]])
numericInput('clusters', 'Cluster count', 3, min = 1, max = 9)
```

```{r}
#| panel: fill
plotOutput('plot1')
```

```{r}
#| context: server
selectedData <- reactive({
    iris[, c(input$xcol, input$ycol)]
  })

clusters <- reactive({
  kmeans(selectedData(), input$clusters)
})

output$plot1 <- renderPlot({
  palette(c("#E41A1C", "#377EB8", "#4DAF4A", "#984EA3",
    "#FF7F00", "#FFFF33", "#A65628", "#F781BF", "#999999"))

  par(mar = c(5.1, 4.1, 0, 1))
  plot(selectedData(),
       col = clusters()$cluster,
       pch = 20, cex = 3)
  points(clusters()$centers, pch = 4, cex = 4, lwd = 4)
})
```
```

--------------------------------

### GET /document-inspection

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/advanced/inspect/index.llms

Retrieves the structural metadata and configuration details of a Quarto document.

```APIDOC
## GET /document-inspection

### Description
Returns the inspection schema object for a Quarto document, containing versioning, engine usage, format configurations, and file-level metadata.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/document-inspection

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **quarto** (object) - The version of Quarto used to inspect the document.
- **engines** (array) - The engines used in the document.
- **formats** (object) - An object representing the formats used in the document (keys) and their configuration (values).
- **resources** (array) - The resource files explicitly provided in the document.
- **fileInformation** (object) - Detailed information about files, including include maps and code cells.
- **project** (object) - Project-level configuration details.

#### Response Example
{
  "quarto": { "version": "1.4.0" },
  "engines": ["markdown", "jupyter"],
  "formats": { "html": { "theme": "default" } },
  "resources": ["data.csv"],
  "fileInformation": {
    "main.qmd": {
      "codeCells": [
        { "start": 10, "end": 15, "language": "python", "source": "print('hello')" }
      ]
    }
  }
}
```

### Latexmk Configuration

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/reference/formats/presentations/beamer.llms

Settings for controlling the LaTeX compilation process, including automatic package installation and compilation passes.

```APIDOC
## Latexmk Configuration

### Description
Settings for Quarto's PDF rendering wrapper and LaTeX compilation behavior.

### Parameters
- **latex-auto-mk** (boolean) - Optional - Use built-in PDF rendering wrapper.
- **latex-auto-install** (boolean) - Optional - Enable/disable automatic LaTeX package installation.
- **latex-min-runs** (number) - Optional - Minimum compilation passes.
- **latex-max-runs** (number) - Optional - Maximum compilation passes.
- **latex-clean** (boolean) - Optional - Clean intermediates after compilation.
- **latex-makeindex** (string) - Optional - Program for makeindex.
- **latex-makeindex-opts** (array) - Optional - Options for makeindex.
- **latex-tlmgr-opts** (array) - Optional - Options for tlmgr.
- **latex-output-dir** (string) - Optional - Output directory for intermediates and PDF.
- **latex-tinytex** (boolean) - Optional - Prevent installation of TinyTex.
- **latex-input-paths** (array) - Optional - Paths LaTeX should search for inputs.
```

### Serve Options for Custom Preview Servers

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/reference/projects/options.llms

Configure `preview: serve` for projects using external preview servers like Hugo or Docusaurus. Specify the command, environment variables, and readiness detection.

```yaml
project:
  type: default
    preview:
      serve:
        cmd: "hugo serve --port {port} --bind {host} --navigateToChanged"
        env:
          HUGO_RELATIVEURLS: "true"
        ready: "Web Server is available at"
```

### Configure Scroll View Options

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/presentations/revealjs/presenting.llms

Use these options under `scroll-view` to configure the scrollable presentation experience. This example sets a compact layout, proximity snap mode, always shows the progress scrollbar, and disables automatic activation for small screens.

```yaml
---
title: "Presentation"
format:
  revealjs:
    scroll-view:
      layout: compact
      snap: proximity
      progress: true
      activation-width: 0
---

```

### Publish Quarto Project with R and renv

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/publishing/quarto-pub.llms

This action installs R and project dependencies using renv.lock, then renders and publishes your Quarto project. Requires QUARTO_PUB_AUTH_TOKEN to be configured in GitHub secrets.

```yaml
on:
  workflow_dispatch:
  push:
    branches: main

name: Quarto Publish

jobs:
  build-deploy:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Check out repository
        uses: actions/checkout@v4 

      - name: Set up Quarto
        uses: quarto-dev/quarto-actions/setup@v2
        
      - name: Install R
        uses: r-lib/actions/setup-r@v2
        with:
          r-version: '4.2.0'
      
      - name: Install R Dependencies 
        uses: r-lib/actions/setup-renv@v2
        with:
          cache-version: 1
      
      - name: Render and Publish
        uses: quarto-dev/quarto-actions/publish@v2
        with:
          target: quarto-pub
          QUARTO_PUB_AUTH_TOKEN: ${{ secrets.QUARTO_PUB_AUTH_TOKEN }}
```

--------------------------------

### DokuWiki Configuration Options

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/reference/formats/wiki/dokuwiki.llms

Overview of available configuration keys for DokuWiki output in Quarto.

```APIDOC
## DokuWiki Configuration

### Description
Configuration options for the DokuWiki output format in Quarto.

### Parameters
#### Metadata Options
- **title** (string) - Document title
- **date** (string) - Document date
- **date-format** (string) - Date format for the document
- **author** (string) - Author or authors of the document
- **order** (integer) - Order for document when included in a website automatic sidebar menu

#### Numbering
- **number-sections** (boolean) - Number section headings. Sections with class .unnumbered will never be numbered.
- **shift-heading-level-by** (integer) - Shift heading levels by a positive or negative integer.

#### Code
- **code-annotations** (boolean/string) - The style to use when displaying code annotations. Set to false to hide.

#### Cross-References
- **crossref** (object) - Configuration for cross-reference labels and prefixes.

#### Rendering
- **from** (string) - Format to read from (e.g., markdown+emoji).
- **output-file** (string) - Output file to write to.
- **output-ext** (string) - Extension to use for generated output file.
- **template** (string) - Custom template file for the generated document.
- **template-partials** (list) - Files to include as partials.
- **filters** (list) - Executables or Lua scripts to transform the pandoc AST.
- **shortcodes** (list) - Lua scripts that implement shortcode handlers.
- **keep-md** (boolean) - Keep the markdown file generated by executing code.
- **keep-ipynb** (boolean) - Keep the notebook file generated from executing code.
- **dpi** (integer) - Default dpi value for conversion (default: 96).
```

### GitHub Action for Knitr with renv

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/publishing/rstudio-connect.llms

This GitHub Action installs R and package dependencies from renv.lock, then renders and publishes the Quarto project to Connect.

```yaml
on:
  workflow_dispatch:
  push:
    branches: main

name: Quarto Publish

jobs:
  build-deploy:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Check out repository
        uses: actions/checkout@v4 

      - name: Set up Quarto
        uses: quarto-dev/quarto-actions/setup@v2
        
      - name: Install R
        uses: r-lib/actions/setup-r@v2
        with:
          r-version: '4.2.0'
      
      - name: Install R Dependencies 
        uses: r-lib/actions/setup-renv@v2
        with:
          cache-version: 1
      
      - name: Render and Publish
        uses: quarto-dev/quarto-actions/publish@v2
        with:
          target: connect
          CONNECT_SERVER: https://connect.example.com
          CONNECT_API_KEY: ${{ secrets.CONNECT_API_KEY }}
```

### GitHub Action: Knitr with renv for Quarto Publish

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/publishing/netlify.llms

This GitHub Action sets up R, installs R package dependencies using `renv.lock`, and publishes Quarto content to Netlify. Ensure `renv.lock` is committed to your repository.

```yaml
on:
  workflow_dispatch:
  push:
    branches: main

name: Quarto Publish

jobs:
  build-deploy:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Check out repository
        uses: actions/checkout@v4 

      - name: Set up Quarto
        uses: quarto-dev/quarto-actions/setup@v2
        
      - name: Install R
        uses: r-lib/actions/setup-r@v2
        with:
          r-version: '4.2.0'
      
      - name: Install R Dependencies 
        uses: r-lib/actions/setup-renv@v2
        with:
          cache-version: 1
      
      - name: Render and Publish
        uses: quarto-dev/quarto-actions/publish@v2
        with:
          target: netlify
          NETLIFY_AUTH_TOKEN: ${{ secrets.NETLIFY_AUTH_TOKEN }}
```

## PDF Compilation Options

### Description
Configuration settings for the built-in PDF engine.

### Parameters
- **latex-min-runs** (Number) - Minimum number of compilation passes.
- **latex-max-runs** (Number) - Maximum number of compilation passes.
- **latex-clean** (Boolean) - Clean intermediates after compilation (default: true).
- **latex-output-dir** (String) - Output directory for intermediates and PDF.
- **latex-makeindex** (String) - Program to use for makeindex.
- **latex-makeindex-opts** (Array) - Options for makeindex program.

## Package Installation Options

### Parameters
- **latex-auto-install** (Boolean) - Enable/disable automatic package installation.
- **latex-tlmgr-opts** (Array) - Options for tlmgr.
```

### quarto add

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/cli/add.llms

Adds an extension to the current folder or project. Extensions can be installed from GitHub repositories, local file paths, or URLs.

```APIDOC
## POST /quarto/add

### Description
Adds an extension to this folder or project.

### Method
POST

### Endpoint
/quarto/add

### Parameters
#### Query Parameters
- **extension** (string) - Required - The name or path of the extension to add. This can be a GitHub repository (e.g., "<gh-org>/<gh-repo>"), a local path to a zip file, or a URL.

### Request Example
```json
{
  "extension": "<extension:string>"
}
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **message** (string) - Confirmation message indicating the extension was added successfully.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "message": "Extension '<extension_name>' added successfully."
}
```

## Options for 'quarto add'

### Description
These options modify the behavior of the 'quarto add' command.

### Method
POST

### Endpoint
/quarto/add

### Parameters
#### Query Parameters
- **-h, --help** (boolean) - Optional - Show this help message.
- **--no-prompt** (boolean) - Optional - Do not prompt to confirm actions.
- **--embed** (boolean) - Optional - Embed this extension within another extension (used when authoring extensions).
- **--log** (string) - Optional - Path to the log file.
- **--log-level** (string) - Optional - Log level (debug, info, warning, error, critical).
- **--log-format** (string) - Optional - Log format (plain, json-stream).
- **--quiet** (boolean) - Optional - Suppress console output.
- **--profile** (string) - Optional - Active project profile(s).

### Request Example
```json
{
  "extension": "<extension:string>",
  "no_prompt": true,
  "embed": false
}
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **message** (string) - Confirmation message indicating the action was completed.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "message": "Extension added with specified options."
}
```

## Examples of 'quarto add'

### Install extension (Github)

```bash
quarto add <gh-org>/<gh-repo>
```

### Install extension (file)

```bash
quarto add <path-to-zip>
```

### Install extension (url)

```bash
quarto add <url>
```
```

### Project Preview Configuration

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/reference/projects/options.llms

Defines the configuration options for the 'quarto preview' command, allowing customization of ports, hosts, and browser behavior.

```APIDOC
## Project Preview Configuration

### Description
Controls the behavior of the Quarto preview server, including network settings and browser automation.

### Parameters
#### Request Body
- **port** (integer) - Optional - Port to listen on (defaults to random value between 3000 and 8000)
- **host** (string) - Optional - Hostname to bind to (defaults to 127.0.0.1)
- **browser** (boolean) - Optional - Open a web browser to view the preview (defaults to true)
- **watch-inputs** (boolean) - Optional - Re-render input files when they change (defaults to true)
- **navigate** (boolean) - Optional - Navigate the browser automatically when outputs are updated (defaults to true)
- **timeout** (integer) - Optional - Time in seconds after which to exit if there are no active clients

### Request Example
project:
  preview:
    port: 4200
    browser: false
```

### Basic Python Computations in Quarto

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/get-started/computations/neovim.llms

Demonstrates basic NumPy array creation, Matplotlib plotting, and Plotly interactive chart generation within a Quarto document. Ensure Python 3 and necessary libraries (numpy, matplotlib, plotly) are installed.

```python
import numpy as np
a = np.arange(15).reshape(3, 5)
a
```

```python
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

fig = plt.figure()
x = np.arange(10)
y = 2.5 * np.sin(x / 20 * np.pi)
yerr = np.linspace(0.05, 0.2, 10)

plt.errorbar(x, y + 3, yerr=yerr, label='both limits (default)')
plt.errorbar(x, y + 2, yerr=yerr, uplims=True, label='uplims=True')
plt.errorbar(x, y + 1, yerr=yerr, uplims=True, lolims=True,
             label='uplims=True, lolims=True')

upperlimits = [True, False] * 5
lowerlimits = [False, True] * 5
plt.errorbar(x, y, yerr=yerr, uplims=upperlimits, lolims=lowerlimits,
             label='subsets of uplims and lolims')

plt.legend(loc='lower right')
plt.show(fig)
```

```python
import plotly.express as px
import plotly.io as pio
gapminder = px.data.gapminder()
gapminder2007 = gapminder.query("year == 2007")
fig = px.scatter(gapminder2007, 
                 x="gdpPercap", y="lifeExp", color="continent", 
                 size="pop", size_max=60,
                 hover_name="country")
fig.show()
```

### GitHub Actions Workflow for Quarto Publish

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/publishing/rstudio-connect.llms

A sample GitHub Actions workflow file (`.github/workflows/publish.yml`) that sets up Quarto, checks out the repository, and renders/publishes content to Posit Connect.

```yaml
on:
  workflow_dispatch:
  push:
    branches: main

name: Quarto Publish

jobs:
  build-deploy:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Check out repository
        uses: actions/checkout@v4 

      - name: Set up Quarto
        uses: quarto-dev/quarto-actions/setup@v2

      - name: Render and Publish 
        uses: quarto-dev/quarto-actions/publish@v2
        with:
          target: connect
          CONNECT_SERVER: https://connect.example.com
          CONNECT_API_KEY: ${{ secrets.CONNECT_API_KEY }}
```

### Accessing Execution Information in Julia

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/advanced/quarto-execute-info.llms

Provides a Julia example for accessing Quarto's execution context by reading the JSON file specified by the QUARTO_EXECUTE_INFO environment variable.

```APIDOC
## Accessing Execution Information in Julia

### Description
This Julia code snippet explains how to access Quarto's execution context. It reads the `QUARTO_EXECUTE_INFO` environment variable to find the JSON metadata file and then parses it to retrieve details about the document and its format.

### Method
Environment Variable Access and File I/O

### Endpoint
N/A (Environment Variable)

### Parameters
#### Environment Variables
- **QUARTO_EXECUTE_INFO** (string) - Required - Path to the JSON file containing execution metadata.

### Request Example
```julia
using JSON

info = JSON.parsefile(ENV["QUARTO_EXECUTE_INFO"])

# Access document path
println(info["document-path"])

# Access format information
println(info["format"]["identifier"]["target-format"])
```

### Response
#### Success Response (stdout)
- **document-path** (string) - The absolute path to the source document being rendered.
- **target-format** (string) - The target output format identifier (e.g., “gfm”, “html”).

#### Response Example
```
/path/to/your/document.qmd
github
```
```

### Separate Server Logic into server.R

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/interactive/shiny/execution.llms

Moves server-side logic into a dedicated file while keeping the .qmd file focused on UI rendering.

```markdown
---
title: "Old Faithful"
format: html
server: shiny
---

```{r}
sliderInput("bins", "Number of bins:", 
            min = 1, max = 50, value = 30)
plotOutput("distPlot")
```
```

```r
function(input, output, session) {
  output$distPlot <- renderPlot({
    x <- faithful[, 2]  # Old Faithful Geyser data
    bins <- seq(min(x), max(x), length.out = input$bins + 1)
    hist(x, breaks = bins, col = 'darkgray', border = 'white')
  })
}
```

### Render and Preview a Quarto Document

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/get-started/hello/vscode.llms

This snippet shows a basic Quarto document structure with YAML front matter and a Python code chunk for plotting. It's used to demonstrate rendering and previewing in VS Code. Ensure required Python packages like matplotlib and numpy are installed.

```markdown
---
title: "Quarto Basics"
format:
  html:
    code-fold: true
jupyter: python3
---

For a demonstration of a line plot on a polar axis, see @fig-polar.

```{python}
#| label: fig-polar
#| fig-cap: "A line plot on a polar axis"

import numpy as np
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

r = np.arange(0, 2, 0.01)
theta = 2 * np.pi * r
fig, ax = plt.subplots(
  subplot_kw = {'projection': 'polar'}
)
ax.plot(theta, r)
ax.set_rticks([0.5, 1, 1.5, 2])
ax.grid(True)
plt.show()
```
```

## Preview Serve Configuration

### Description
Used for integrating external preview servers like Hugo or Docusaurus.

### Parameters
#### Request Body
- **cmd** (string) - Required - Command to serve the project preview
- **args** (list) - Optional - Additional command line arguments
- **env** (object) - Optional - Environment variables for the command
- **ready** (string) - Optional - Regular expression for detecting server readiness

### Request Example

preview:

}
```

  { "year": 1959, "max": 317.51 },

### Configure LaTeX Index with makeidx

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/books/book-structure.llms

Add LaTeX makeidx package and commands to PDF output configuration in _quarto.yml for creating an index.

```yaml
format:
  html:
    theme: cosmo
  pdf:
    documentclass: scrreprt
    include-in-header:
      text: |
        \usepackage{makeidx}
        \makeindex
    include-after-body:
      text: |
        \printindex
```

## Serve Options

### Description
Customize the behavior of the preview server when using an external publishing system.

### Parameters
#### Request Body
- **project.preview.serve** (object) - Optional - Serve project preview configuration.
  - **cmd** (string) - Required - Serve project preview using the specified command. Interpolate the `--port` into the command using `{port}`.
  - **args** (array of strings) - Optional - Additional command line arguments for preview command.
  - **env** (object) - Optional - Environment variables to set for preview command.
  - **ready** (string) - Optional - Regular expression for detecting when the server is ready.

### Add Subscription Widget HTML to Quarto Project

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/websites/website-blog.llms

Example HTML for a Mailchimp subscription widget. This HTML should be placed in a `subscribe.html` file in your project's root and configured in `_quarto.yml`.

```html
<span style="font-weight: 600;">Subscribe</span>

<!-- Begin Mailchimp Signup Form -->
<link href="http://cdn-images.mailchimp.com/embedcode/slim-10_7_dtp.css" rel="stylesheet" type="text/css">
<style type="text/css">
    #mc_embed_signup{background:#fff; clear:left; font:14px Helvetica,Arial,sans-serif;  width:170px;}
    /* Add your own Mailchimp form style overrides in your site stylesheet or in this style block. 
       We recommend moving this block and the preceding CSS link to the HEAD of your HTML file. */
    #mc-embedded-subscribe-form{margin-left:-5px;}
</style>
<div id="mc_embed_signup">
<form action="<site_url>" method="post" id="mc-embedded-subscribe-form" name="mc-embedded-subscribe-form" class="validate" target="_blank" novalidate>
    <div id="mc_embed_signup_scroll">

    <input type="email" value="" name="EMAIL" class="email" id="mce-EMAIL" placeholder="email address" required>
    <!-- real people should not fill this in and expect good things - do not remove this or risk form bot signups-->
    <div style="position: absolute; left: -5000px;" aria-hidden="true"><input type="text" name="b_f718424fc5df77c22533bdaa6_a3c37fb57b" tabindex="-1" value=""></div>
        <div class="optionalParent">
            <div class="clear foot" style="margin-top: 10px;">
                <input type="submit" value="Subscribe" name="subscribe" id="mc-embedded-subscribe" class="button">
                <p class="brandingLogo"></p>
            </div>
        </div>
    </div>
</form>
</div>

<!--End mc_embed_signup-->

```

### Create a Plot with ObservableJS

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/interactive/ojs/examples/layout.llms

Generate visualizations using the Plot library. This example creates a bar chart showing counts of penguins binned by body mass, faceted by sex and species.

```javascript
Plot.rectY(filtered, 
  Plot.binX(
    {y: "count"}, 
    {x: "body_mass_g", fill: "species", thresholds: 20}
  ))
  .plot({
    facet: {
      data: filtered,
      x: "sex",
      y: "species",
      marginRight: 80
    },
    marks: [
      Plot.frame(),
    ]
  }
)

```

### Automate Quarto Report Rendering with Python

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/blog/posts/2025-07-24-parameterized-reports-python/index.llms

Iterate through a DataFrame of cities and their output files to render Quarto notebooks programmatically using the 'quarto' Python package. Ensure the 'quarto' package is installed.

```python
from quarto import render
for row in cities.iter_rows(named=True):
    render(
        "climate.ipynb",
        execute_params={"city": row["city"]},
        output_file=row["output_file"],
    )
```

### Project Serve Configuration

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/reference/projects/options.llms

Defines configuration for external preview servers used by project extensions.

```APIDOC
## Project Serve Configuration

### Description
Customizes the behavior of external preview servers (e.g., Hugo, Docusaurus) integrated into a Quarto project.

### Parameters
#### Request Body
- **cmd** (string) - Required - Serve project preview using the specified command. Use {port} and {host} for interpolation.
- **args** (array) - Optional - Additional command line arguments for preview command.
- **env** (object) - Optional - Environment variables to set for preview command.
- **ready** (string) - Optional - Regular expression for detecting when the server is ready.

### Request Example
project:
  preview:
    serve:
      cmd: "hugo serve --port {port} --bind {host}"
      env:
        HUGO_RELATIVEURLS: "true"
      ready: "Web Server is available at"
```

  - attribution
---

--------------------------------

### Example Footnote Syntax

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/authoring/markdown-basics.llms

Define footnotes using `[^identifier]` syntax. Multi-paragraph footnotes can be created by indenting subsequent paragraphs.

```markdown
[^1]: Here is the footnote.
```

```markdown
[^2]: Here’s one with multiple blocks.

    Subsequent paragraphs are indented to show that they belong to the previous footnote.

        { some.code }

    The whole paragraph can be indented, or just the first line. In this way, multi-paragraph footnotes work like multi-paragraph list items.
```

```markdown
[^3]: Inlines notes are easier to write, since you don’t have to pick an identifier and move down to type the note.
```

```python

```

```markdown
The radius of the circle is `{python} radius`

--------------------------------

### Creating a Histogram with Observable Plot

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/interactive/ojs/libraries.llms

This example demonstrates creating a histogram of athlete weights, faceted by sex, using Observable Plot. It requires loading data from a CSV file using `FileAttachment`.

```ojs
athletes = FileAttachment("athletes.csv").csv({typed: true})

Plot.plot({
  grid: true,
  facet: {
    data: athletes,
    y: "sex"
  },
  marks: [
    Plot.rectY(
      athletes, 
      Plot.binX({y: "count"}, {x: "weight", fill: "sex"})
    ),
    Plot.ruleY([0])
  ]
})
```

--------------------------------

### Set Document YAML Options in Quarto

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/get-started/hello/jupyter.llms

Use YAML front matter to define document-level options such as title, format, and Jupyter kernel. This example sets the title to 'Quarto Basics' and configures HTML output with code folding enabled.

```yaml
---
title: "Quarto Basics"
format:
  html:
    code-fold: true
jupyter: python3
---
```

### Quarto Prerelease Builds

Source: https://quarto.org/llms.txt

This section provides information on accessing prerelease builds of Quarto. It typically involves downloading a specific version from a designated URL.

```bash
wget https://github.com/quarto-dev/quarto-cli/releases/download/v1.5.25-rc1/quarto-1.5.25-rc1-linux-amd64.tar.gz
tar -xzf quarto-1.5.25-rc1-linux-amd64.tar.gz
sudo mv quarto-1.5.25-rc1/bin/quarto /usr/local/bin/
sudo rm -rf quarto-1.5.25-rc1 quarto-1.5.25-rc1-linux-amd64.tar.gz
```

### Quarto Call Engine Julia Status Command

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/cli/call.llms

Get status information on the currently running Julia server process.

```APIDOC
## quarto call engine julia status

### Description
Get status information on the currently running Julia server process.

### Method
CLI

### Endpoint
N/A (CLI command)

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
N/A

#### Query Parameters
N/A

#### Request Body
N/A

### Request Example
```bash
quarto call engine julia status 
```

### Response
N/A (CLI command output varies)

### Options
- `-h`, `--help`: Show this help.
- `--log`: Path to log file
- `--log-level`: Log level (info, warning, error, critical)
- `--log-format`: Log format (plain, json-stream)
- `--quiet`: Suppress console output.
- `--profile`: Active project profile(s)

### Commands
- `help`: Show this help or the help of a sub-command.
```

### R Code Annotation Syntax Example

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/blog/posts/2023-03-13-code-annotation/index.llms

Illustrates the exact syntax for adding code annotations in R. Each annotated line ends with a comment containing '<number>', and a corresponding ordered list follows the code block.

```r
library(tidyverse)
library(palmerpenguins)
penguins |>                                      # <1>
  mutate(                                        # <2>
    bill_ratio = bill_depth_mm / bill_length_mm, # <2>
    bill_area  = bill_depth_mm * bill_length_mm  # <2>
  )                                              # <2>
```

--------------------------------

### Quarto Check Command

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/cli/check.llms

The 'quarto check' command verifies the correct functioning of your Quarto installation. You can specify a target to check specific functionality.

```APIDOC
## quarto check [target:string]

### Description
Verifies correct functioning of Quarto installation. Check specific functionality with argument install, jupyter, knitr, or all.

### Method
CLI

### Endpoint
N/A (CLI Command)

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
- **target** (string) - Required - The specific functionality to check (e.g., install, jupyter, knitr, all).

#### Query Parameters
- **--output** (string) - Optional - Output as JSON to a file.
- **--no-strict** (boolean) - Optional - When set, will not fail if dependency versions don't match precisely.
- **--log** (string) - Optional - Path to log file.
- **--log-level** (string) - Optional - Log level (debug, info, warning, error, critical).
- **--log-format** (string) - Optional - Log format (plain, json-stream).
- **--quiet** (boolean) - Optional - Suppress console output.
- **--profile** (string) - Optional - Active project profile(s).

### Request Example
```bash
quarto check install
quarto check jupyter
quarto check knitr
quarto check all
quarto check --output report.json
```

### Response
#### Success Response (0)
- **Output**: Console output indicating the status of the check.

#### Response Example
```
Quarto installation check successful.
```

### Error Handling
- **Non-zero exit code**: Indicates an error during the check process.
```

--------------------------------

### BibTeX Citation Entry

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/manuscripts/authoring/jupyterlab.llms

An example of a single citation entry in a .bib file. Ensure your .bib file contains all necessary citation details.

```bibtex
@article{marrero2019,
  author = {Marrero, Jos{\'e} and Garc{\'i}a, Alicia and Berrocoso, Manuel and Llinares, {\'A}ngeles and Rodr{\'i}guez-Losada, Antonio and Ortiz, R.},
  journal = {Journal of Applied Volcanology},
  year = {2019},
  month = {7},
  pages = {},
  title = {Strategies for the development of volcanic hazard maps in monogenetic volcanic fields: the example of {La} {Palma} ({Canary} {Islands})},
  volume = {8},
  doi = {10.1186/s13617-019-0085-5},
}
```

### Displaying Palmer Penguins Data with Observable JS

Source: https://quarto.org/llms.txt

This example demonstrates how to display the Palmer Penguins dataset using Observable JS within a Quarto document. It requires the 'penguins' data to be available.

```html
<div id="penguins"></div>
<script type="module">
import * as d3 from "https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/npm/d3@7"
import { penguins } from "./penguins.js"

d3.select("#penguins").append(() => penguins())
</script>
```

### Custom Format Extension Configuration

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/extensions/formats.llms

The `_extension.yml` file defines the custom format. This example configures a `lexdoc-html` format derived from the base `html` format, enabling TOC and setting a theme with custom SCSS.

```yaml
title: Lexdoc
author: J.J. Allaire
version: 1.0.0
quarto-required: ">=1.2.222"
contributes:
  formats:
    html:
      toc: true
      theme: [yeti, custom.scss]
```

### Revealjs Plugin JavaScript Implementation

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/extensions/revealjs.llms

Implement plugin functionality in `shuffler.js`. The `init` function receives the Revealjs deck instance, allowing you to add event listeners or modify deck behavior. This example adds a key binding to shuffle slides.

```javascript
window.RevealShuffler = function () {
  return {
    id: "RevealShuffler",
    init: function (deck) {
      // TODO: Implement your plugin functionality
      // Learn more at https://revealjs.com/creating-plugins/
      
      // This example shuffles the deck when the 'T' key is pressed
      deck.addKeyBinding({ keyCode: 84, key: "T" }, () => {
        deck.shuffle();
      });
    },
  };
};

```

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/authoring/markdown-basics.llms

This is how Quarto renders a simple div with a class to an HTML `<div>` element. The content within the div is preserved.

<div class="border">
  <p>This content can be styled with a border</p>
</div>

--------------------------------

### Specify Julia Version with juliaup

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/computations/julia.llms

Use the `+` channel specifier in the notebook frontmatter's `julia.exeflags` option to select a specific Julia version managed by juliaup. This allows concurrent notebooks to use different Julia versions without PATH modifications. Requires juliaup to have the desired channels installed.

```yaml
---
title: "A Julia 1.11 notebook"
engine: julia
julia:
  exeflags: ["+1.11"]
---

```{julia}
VERSION
```
```

### Content Visible in HTML and Not Reveal.js

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/authoring/conditional.llms

```markdown
::: {.content-visible when-format="html" unless-format="revealjs"}

Will only appear in HTML and not in Reveal.js, but actually it appears.

:::
```

radius = 10

### Configure PDF Output Options

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/output-formats/pdf-basics.llms

Customize PDF output by specifying document class, page geometry, fonts, and enabling lists of figures and tables. This example uses 'report' class with two-column landscape layout.

```yaml
---
title: "My Document"
format: 
  pdf: 
    documentclass: report
    classoption: [twocolumn, landscape]
    lof: true
    lot: true
    geometry:
      - top=30mm
      - left=20mm
      - heightrounded
    mainfont: Times New Roman
    colorlinks: true
---

```

### R Markdown with ggplot2

Source: https://quarto.org/index.llms

Example of creating a plot using ggplot2 in R within a Quarto document. The code folding is enabled for the R chunk.

```markdown
---
title: "ggplot2 demo"
author: "Norah Jones"
date: "5/22/2021"
format: 
  html:
    fig-width: 8
    fig-height: 4
    code-fold: true
---

## Air Quality

@fig-airquality further explores the impact of temperature on ozone level.

```{r}
#| label: fig-airquality
#| fig-cap: "Temperature and ozone level."
#| warning: false

library(ggplot2)
ggplot(airquality, aes(Temp, Ozone)) + 
  geom_point() + 
  geom_smooth(method = "loess")
```
```

### R Code Annotation Example

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/authoring/code-annotation.llms

Demonstrates adding line-based annotations to an R dplyr pipeline. Annotations are marked with '# <number>' and explained in a list below the code.

```r
library(tidyverse)
library(palmerpenguins)
penguins |>                                            # <1>
  mutate(                                              # <2>
    bill_ratio = bill_depth_mm / bill_length_mm,       # <2>
    bill_area  = bill_depth_mm * bill_length_mm        # <2>
  )                                                    # <2>
```

### Markdown Figure Cross-Reference

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/authoring/cross-references.llms

```markdown
![Elephant](elephant.png){#fig-elephant}

See @fig-elephant for an illustration.
```

### Configure GitHub Action for Netlify

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/publishing/netlify.llms

Define a workflow file to render and publish a Quarto project to Netlify on push events.

```yaml
on:
  workflow_dispatch:
  push:
    branches: main

name: Quarto Publish

jobs:
  build-deploy:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Check out repository
        uses: actions/checkout@v4 

      - name: Set up Quarto
        uses: quarto-dev/quarto-actions/setup@v2

      - name: Render and Publish 
        uses: quarto-dev/quarto-actions/publish@v2
        with:
          target: netlify
          NETLIFY_AUTH_TOKEN: ${{ secrets.NETLIFY_AUTH_TOKEN }}
```

--------------------------------

```

```bash
quarto render notebook.ipynb --execute
```

### Observable JS Plotting

Source: https://quarto.org/index.llms

Example of creating an interactive plot using Observable JS within a Quarto document. This snippet visualizes Seattle precipitation data.

```markdown
---
title: "observable plot"
author: "Norah Jones"
format: 
  html: 
    code-fold: true
---

## Seattle Precipitation by Day (2012 to 2016)

```{ojs}
data = FileAttachment("seattle-weather.csv")
  .csv({typed: true})
  
Plot.plot({
  width: 800, height: 500, padding: 0,
  color: { scheme: "blues", type: "sqrt"},
  y: { tickFormat: i => "JFMAMJJASOND"[i] },
  marks: [
    Plot.cell(data, Plot.group({fill: "mean"}, {
      x: d => new Date(d.date).getDate(),
      y: d => new Date(d.date).getMonth(),
      fill: "precipitation", 
      inset: 0.5
    }))
  ]
})
```
```

```bash
quarto render notebook.ipynb --to docx,pdf
```

### Element Matching with Data-ID

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/presentations/revealjs/advanced.llms

Use the `data-id` attribute to explicitly match elements for animation when automatic matching is insufficient. This example also demonstrates `auto-animate-easing` and `auto-animate-delay`.

```markdown
## {auto-animate=true auto-animate-easing="ease-in-out"}

::: {.r-hstack}
::: {data-id="box1" auto-animate-delay="0" style="background: #2780e3; width: 200px; height: 150px; margin: 10px;"}
:::

::: {data-id="box2" auto-animate-delay="0.1" style="background: #3fb618; width: 200px; height: 150px; margin: 10px;"}
:::

::: {data-id="box3" auto-animate-delay="0.2" style="background: #e83e8c; width: 200px; height: 150px; margin: 10px;"}
:::
:::

## {auto-animate=true auto-animate-easing="ease-in-out"}

::: {.r-stack}
::: {data-id="box1" style="background: #2780e3; width: 350px; height: 350px; border-radius: 200px;"}
:::

::: {data-id="box2" style="background: #3fb618; width: 250px; height: 250px; border-radius: 200px;"}
:::

::: {data-id="box3" style="background: #e83e8c; width: 150px; height: 150px; border-radius: 200px;"}
:::
:::

```

### Quarto Conditional Blocks Custom Node API Example

```html
<div id="conditional-block-custom-node"></div>
<script type="module">
import { conditional_block } from "./conditional-block.js"

d3.select("#conditional-block-custom-node").append(() => conditional_block())
</script>
```

### Configure LaTeX Index with imakeidx

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/books/book-structure.llms

Configure PDF output in _quarto.yml to use the imakeidx package with advanced options for index formatting.

```yaml
format:
  html:
    theme: cosmo
  pdf:
    documentclass: scrreprt
    include-in-header:
      text: |
        \usepackage{imakeidx}
        \makeindex[intoc=true, columns=3, columnseprule=true, options=-s latex/indexstyles.ist]
    include-after-body:
      text: |
        \printindex
```

--------------------------------

### Custom Float Cross-Reference Type

Source: https://quarto.org/llms.txt

This example defines a custom float cross-reference type named 'algorithm' in Quarto. It specifies the label and caption format for this new type.

```yaml
---
format:
  html:
    crossref:
      fig-title: "Figure {. {#fig}}"
      tbl-title: "Table {. {#tbl}}"
      lst-title: "Listing {. {#lst}}"
      eqn-title: "Equation {. {#eq}}"
      sec-title: "Section {. {#sec}}"
      autolabel: true
      # Custom float types
      alg-title: "Algorithm {. {#alg}}"
---

# My Document

Here is an algorithm:

```{=latex}
\begin{algorithm}
  \label{alg:my-algorithm}
  % algorithm content
\end{algorithm}
```

See Algorithm @alg-my-algorithm.
```

### Define a Cross-Referenceable Table with Markdown

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/authoring/cross-references-divs.llms

Create a cross-referenceable table by using a fenced div with an ID starting with 'tbl-'. The markdown table and its caption should be placed inside the div.

```markdown
::: {#tbl-letters}

| Col1 | Col2 | Col3 |
|------|------|------|
| A    | B    | C    |
| E    | F    | G    |
| A    | G    | G    |

My Caption

:::
```

--------------------------------

### Configure LaTeX output format

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/output-formats/pdf-basics.llms

Set the format to latex to produce a .tex file instead of a PDF.

```yaml
format:
  latex:
    documentclass: report
    classoption: [twocolumn, landscape]
    lof: true
    lot: true
```

--------------------------------

### Define a Cross-Referenceable Figure with an Image

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/authoring/cross-references-divs.llms

To create a cross-referenceable figure, use a fenced div with an ID starting with 'fig-'. Include the image markdown and the caption within the div.

```markdown
::: {#fig-elephant}

![](elephant.png)

An Elephant
:::
```

### CLI: quarto inspect

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/cli/inspect.llms

Inspects a Quarto project or input path and returns configuration and metadata.

```APIDOC
## CLI COMMAND: quarto inspect

### Description
Inspects a Quarto project or input path. Inspecting a project returns its config and engines, while inspecting an input path returns its formats, engine, and dependent resources.

### Usage
`quarto inspect [path] [output]`

### Parameters
#### Positional Arguments
- **path** (string) - Optional - The path to the Quarto project or input file. Defaults to current directory.
- **output** (string) - Optional - The file path to write the JSON inspection results. If not provided, results are emitted to stdout.

#### Options
- **-h, --help** - Show help.
- **--log** (string) - Path to log file.
- **--log-level** (string) - Log level (debug, info, warning, error, critical).
- **--log-format** (string) - Log format (plain, json-stream).
- **--quiet** - Suppress console output.
- **--profile** (string) - Active project profile(s).

### Examples
- Inspect project in current directory: `quarto inspect`
- Inspect project in directory: `quarto inspect myproject`
- Inspect input path: `quarto inspect document.md`
- Inspect input path and write to file: `quarto inspect document.md output.json`
```

--------------------------------

### Nested Fragment Effects

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/presentations/revealjs/advanced.llms

Apply multiple fragment effects sequentially to a single element by nesting fragment definitions. This example demonstrates fading in, then turning red, then partially fading out.

```markdown
::: {.fragment .fade-in}
::: {.fragment .highlight-red}
::: {.fragment .semi-fade-out}
Fade in > Turn red > Semi fade out
:::
:::
:::
```

### Embed Leaflet Map in Quarto

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/interactive/widgets/htmlwidgets.llms

library(leaflet)

  addTiles() %>%

### Clone Repository and Create Branch

Source: https://quarto.org/about.llms

Use these bash commands to clone your forked repository, configure it for your platform, and checkout a new branch for your feature.

```bash
# clone your fork
$ git clone https://github.com/<username>/quarto-cli

# configure for your platform (./configure.sh or ./configure.cmd for windows)
$ cd quarto-cli
$ ./configure.sh

# checkout a new branch
$ git checkout -b feature/newthing
```

```markdown
## Shortcuts & Options

### Keyboard Shortcuts

*   `Ctrl+B` / `Cmd+B`: Bold
*   `Ctrl+I` / `Cmd+I`: Italic
*   `Ctrl+K` / `Cmd+K`: Insert Link

### Editor Options

*   **Theme:** Choose between light and dark themes.
*   **Font Size:** Adjust the text size for readability.

### Define Render and Server Contexts in a Single File

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/interactive/shiny/execution.llms

Uses the server: shiny format and context: server chunk option to separate UI definition from server-side reactive logic.

```markdown
---
title: "Old Faithful"
format: html
server: shiny
---

```{r}
sliderInput("bins", "Number of bins:", 
            min = 1, max = 50, value = 30)
plotOutput("distPlot")
```

```{r}
#| context: server
output$distPlot <- renderPlot({
  x <- faithful[, 2]  # Old Faithful Geyser data
  bins <- seq(min(x), max(x), length.out = input$bins + 1)
  hist(x, breaks = bins, col = 'darkgray', border = 'white')
})
```
```

### Renderings with Caption and Cross-reference

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/computations/execution-options.llms

Combine `renderings` with fenced div syntax to include captions and cross-references for plots, noting that cross-reference labels starting with `fig-` or `tbl-` are not compatible with `renderings`.

```r
#| label: caption-crossref
#| renderings: [light, dark]
par(bg = "#FFFFFF", fg = "#000000")
plot(1:10) # Shown in `light` mode


par(bg = "#000000", fg = "#FFFFFF", col.axis = "#FFFFFF")
plot(1:10) # Shown in `dark` mode
```

### Panel Layout with Relative Widths

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/interactive/layout.llms

Specify relative widths for elements within rows of a panel layout using the `layout` attribute. This example demonstrates a 3:2 ratio for the second row.

```default

(outputs)

```

### Quarto Extension: Notebook Filter

Source: https://quarto.org/llms.txt

This example shows a Python function that acts as a notebook filter for Quarto extensions. It processes notebook cells, demonstrating how to modify or inspect cell content.

```python
def filter_notebook_cells(cells):
  for cell in cells:
    if cell['cell_type'] == 'code':
      cell['source'] = '# Filtered: ' + cell['source']
  return cells
```

### Initialize and Render Sunburst Diagram

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/interactive/ojs/examples/sunburst.llms

This snippet handles the creation of the SVG, the rendering of arcs and labels, and the click-to-zoom interaction logic.

```js
sunburst = {
  const root = partition(flareData);

  root.each(d => d.current = d);

  const svg = d3.create("svg")
      .attr("viewBox", [0, 0, width, width])
      .style("font", "15px sans-serif");

  const g = svg.append("g")
      .attr("transform", `translate(${width / 2},${width / 2})`);

  const path = g.append("g")
    .selectAll("path")
    .data(root.descendants().slice(1))
    .join("path")
      .attr("fill", d => { while (d.depth > 1) d = d.parent; return color(d.data.name); })
      .attr("fill-opacity", d => arcVisible(d.current) ? (d.children ? 0.6 : 0.4) : 0)
      .attr("d", d => arc(d.current));

  path.filter(d => d.children)
      .style("cursor", "pointer")
      .on("click", clicked);

  path.append("title")
      .text(d => `${d.ancestors().map(d => d.data.name).reverse().join("/")}\n${format(d.value)}`);

  const label = g.append("g")
      .attr("pointer-events", "none")
      .attr("text-anchor", "middle")
      .style("user-select", "none")
    .selectAll("text")
    .data(root.descendants().slice(1))
    .join("text")
      .attr("dy", "0.35em")
      .attr("fill-opacity", d => +labelVisible(d.current))
      .attr("transform", d => labelTransform(d.current))
      .text(d => d.data.name);

  const parent = g.append("circle")
      .datum(root)
      .attr("r", radius)
      .attr("fill", "none")
      .attr("pointer-events", "all")
      .on("click", clicked);

  function clicked(event, p) {
    parent.datum(p.parent || root);

    root.each(d => d.target = {
      x0: Math.max(0, Math.min(1, (d.x0 - p.x0) / (p.x1 - p.x0))) * 2 * Math.PI,
      x1: Math.max(0, Math.min(1, (d.x1 - p.x0) / (p.x1 - p.x0))) * 2 * Math.PI,
      y0: Math.max(0, d.y0 - p.depth),
      y1: Math.max(0, d.y1 - p.depth)
    });

    const t = g.transition().duration(750);

    // Transition the data on all arcs, even the ones that aren’t visible,
    // so that if this transition is interrupted, entering arcs will start
    // the next transition from the desired position.
    path.transition(t)
        .tween("data", d => {
          const i = d3.interpolate(d.current, d.target);
          return t => d.current = i(t);
        })
      .filter(function(d) {
        return +this.getAttribute("fill-opacity") || arcVisible(d.target);
      })
        .attr("fill-opacity", d => arcVisible(d.target) ? (d.children ? 0.6 : 0.4) : 0)
        .attrTween("d", d => () => arc(d.current));

    label.filter(function(d) {
        return +this.getAttribute("fill-opacity") || labelVisible(d.target);
      }).transition(t)
        .attr("fill-opacity", d => +labelVisible(d.target))
        .attrTween("transform", d => () => labelTransform(d.current));
  }
  
  function arcVisible(d) {
    return d.y1 <= 3 && d.y0 >= 1 && d.x1 > d.x0;
  }

  function labelVisible(d) {
    return d.y1 <= 3 && d.y0 >= 1 && (d.y1 - d.y0) * (d.x1 - d.x0) > 0.03;
  }

  function labelTransform(d) {
    const x = (d.x0 + d.x1) / 2 * 180 / Math.PI;
    const y = (d.y0 + d.y1) / 2 * radius;
    return `rotate(${x - 90}) translate(${y},0) rotate(${x < 180 ? 0 : 180})`;
  }

  return svg.node();
}
```

### YAML Front Matter Example

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/manuscripts/authoring/jupyterlab.llms

This YAML header is used to specify scholarly front matter for articles, including title, author details, abstract, and publication information. Ensure correct key-value syntax.

```yaml
title: La Palma Earthquakes
author:
  - name: Steve Purves
    orcid: 0000-0002-0760-5497
    corresponding: true
    email: steve@curvenote.com
    roles:
      - Investigation
      - Project administration
      - Software
      - Visualization
    affiliations:
      - Curvenote
  - name: Rowan Cockett
    orcid: 0000-0002-7859-8394
    corresponding: false
    roles: []
    affiliations:
      - Curvenote
keywords:
  - La Palma
  - Earthquakes
abstract: |
  In September 2021, a significant jump in seismic activity on the island of La Palma (Canary Islands, Spain) signaled the start of a volcanic crisis that still continues at the time of writing. Earthquake data is continually collected and published by the Instituto Geográphico Nacional (IGN). ...
plain-language-summary: |
  Earthquake data for the island of La Palma from the September 2021 eruption is found ...
key-points:
  - A web scraping script was developed to pull data from the Instituto Geogràphico Nacional into a machine-readable form for analysis
  - Earthquake events on La Palma are consistent with the presence of both mantle and crustal reservoirs.
date: last-modified
bibliography: references.bib
citation:
  container-title: Earth and Space Science
number-sections: true

```

### Get Document Metadata in Lua Filter

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/extensions/lua-api.llms

Use `quarto.metadata.get(key)` to retrieve metadata values. The function returns a `pandoc.MetaValue` which can be converted to a string using `pandoc.utils.stringify()` if needed. Check for the existence of metadata before processing.

```lua
function Meta(meta)
  -- Get a simple metadata value
  local title = quarto.metadata.get("title")

  -- Check if a value exists before using it
  local customField = quarto.metadata.get("custom-field")
  if customField then
    -- Process the metadata value
    local value = pandoc.utils.stringify(customField)
  end

  return meta
end
```

```lua
function Pandoc(doc)
  -- Get metadata as MetaValue
  local metaValue = quarto.metadata.get("description")

  -- Convert to string for processing
  local description = pandoc.utils.stringify(metaValue)

  -- Handle complex metadata structures
  local keywords = quarto.metadata.get("keywords")
  if type(keywords) == "table" then
    -- Process as a list or map
    for k, v in pairs(keywords) do
      quarto.log.output(pandoc.utils.stringify(v))
    end
  end

  return doc
end
```

### Quarto Article Layout with Python Plotting

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/get-started/authoring/jupyter.llms

Configure Quarto article layout for HTML output, specifying reference location for footnotes and enabling screen-inset for figures. This example uses Python with Matplotlib to generate plots with colorbars.

```yaml
---
title: Quarto Layout
format: html
reference-location: margin
jupyter: python3
---

```

```python
#| code-fold: true
#| column: screen-inset
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
import numpy as np

fig, axs = plt.subplots(2, 2)
fig.set_size_inches(20, 8)
cmaps = ['RdBu_r', 'viridis']
for col in range(2):
    for row in range(2):
        ax = axs[row, col]
        pcm = ax.pcolormesh(
          np.random.random((20, 20)) * (col + 1),
          cmap=cmaps[col]
        )
        fig.colorbar(pcm, ax=ax)
plt.show()

```

--------------------------------

### Configure GitHub Repository Links in Quarto

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/websites/website-navigation.llms

Add `repo-url` and `repo-actions` to the `website` configuration to include links to the GitHub repository for editing, viewing source, or reporting issues.

```yaml
website:
  repo-url: https://github.com/quarto-dev/quarto-demo
  repo-actions: [edit, source, issue]
```

### Add Cell Attributes (colspan, rowspan) to List Table

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/authoring/tables.llms

Use empty spans with attributes like 'colspan' or 'rowspan' at the start of a cell to control cell spanning. Ensure subsequent rows account for spanned cells.

```markdown
:::.list-table
- - []{colspan=2} Item
  - Price

- - []{rowspan=2} Citrus
  - Orange
  - 0.90

- - Lemon
  - 0.80

- - []{rowspan=2} Stone Fruit
  - Peach
  - 1.20

- - Plum
  - 1.00
:::
```

```bash
quarto preview document.qmd
```

```bash
quarto preview notebook.qmd --to pdf
```

--------------------------------

### Prepend Comment to Code Cells

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/extensions/nbfilter.llms

This Python script uses the nbformat package to read a notebook from stdin, prepend a comment to each code cell's source, and write the modified notebook to stdout. Ensure the nbformat package is installed.

```python
import sys
import nbformat

# read notebook from stdin
nb = nbformat.reads(sys.stdin.read(), as_version = 4)

# prepend a comment to the source of each cell
for index, cell in enumerate(nb.cells):
  if cell.cell_type == 'code':
     cell.source = "# comment\n" + cell.source
  
# write notebook to stdout 
nbformat.write(nb, sys.stdout)
```

### Render a Dynamic Plot with Seaborn

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/dashboards/interactivity/shiny-python/index.llms

Use the `@render.plot` decorator to create dynamic plots that automatically update based on user input. This example uses Seaborn for plotting and retrieves input values via `input.x()`, `input.rug()`, and `input.dist()`.

```python
@render.plot
def displot():
    sns.displot(
        data=penguins, hue="species", multiple="stack",
        x=input.x(), rug=input.rug(), kind=input.dist())

```
