### Include Quarto Markdown in LaTeX Raw Blocks

Source: https://quarto.org/llms.txt

This example shows how to embed Quarto Markdown content within a LaTeX raw block. This allows for mixing Quarto's rendering capabilities with LaTeX's typesetting features.

```markdown
---
format: pdf
---

This is regular Quarto content.

```{=latex}
\documentclass{article}
\begin{document}

This is LaTeX content.

# Quarto Content Inside LaTeX

This content is rendered by Quarto within a LaTeX raw block.

\end{document}
```

This is more regular Quarto content.
```

### Declare a Cross-Referenceable Float with Div Syntax

```markdown

CONTENT

Caption

:::

--------------------------------

### Create a Polar Axis Line Plot with Quarto Code Cell

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/get-started/hello/jupyter.llms

Embed Python code within a Quarto code cell to generate a plot. This example uses numpy and matplotlib to create a line plot on a polar axis, with cell options for labeling and figure captioning.

```python
#| label: fig-polar
#| fig-cap: "A line plot on a polar axis"

import numpy as np
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

r = np.arange(0, 2, 0.01)
theta = 2 * np.pi * r
fig, ax = plt.subplots(
  subplot_kw = {'projection': 'polar'} 
)
ax.plot(theta, r)
ax.set_rticks([0.5, 1, 1.5, 2])
ax.grid(True)
plt.show()
```

### Preview Options

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/reference/projects/books.llms

Specify options that control the behavior of `quarto preview` within the `preview` key.

```APIDOC
## Preview Options

### Description
Options that control the behavior of `quarto preview`.

### Parameters
#### Request Body
- **project.preview** (object) - Optional - Preview configuration options.
  - **port** (integer) - Optional - Port to listen on (defaults to random value between 3000 and 8000).
  - **host** (string) - Optional - Hostname to bind to (defaults to 127.0.0.1).
  - **serve** (object) - Optional - Options for external preview server (see [Serve](#serve)).
  - **browser** (boolean) - Optional - Open a web browser to view the preview (defaults to true).
  - **watch-inputs** (boolean) - Optional - Re-render input files when they change (defaults to true).
  - **navigate** (boolean) - Optional - Navigate the browser automatically when outputs are updated (defaults to true).
  - **timeout** (integer) - Optional - Time (in seconds) after which to exit if there are no active clients.
```

### Configure Data and D3 Helpers

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/interactive/ojs/examples/sunburst.llms

This snippet defines the data loading, partition layout, color scales, and arc generators required for the visualization.

```js
flareData = FileAttachment("flare-2.json").json()

partition = flareData => {
  const root = d3.hierarchy(flareData)
      .sum(d => d.value)
      .sort((a, b) => b.value - a.value);
  return d3.partition()
      .size([2 * Math.PI, root.height + 1])
    (root);
}

color = d3.scaleOrdinal(
  d3.quantize(d3.interpolateRainbow, flareData.children.length + 1)
)

format = d3.format(",d")

width = 932

radius = width / 6

arc = d3.arc()
    .startAngle(d => d.x0)
    .endAngle(d => d.x1)
    .padAngle(d => Math.min((d.x1 - d.x0) / 2, 0.005))
    .padRadius(radius * 1.5)
    .innerRadius(d => d.y0 * radius)
    .outerRadius(d => Math.max(d.y0 * radius, d.y1 * radius - 1))
```

### Revealjs Plugin Configuration (_extension.yml)

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/extensions/revealjs.llms

```yaml
title: Shuffler
author: J.J. Allaire
version: 1.0.0
quarto-required: ">=1.2.222"
contributes:
  revealjs-plugins:
    - name: RevealShuffler
      script:
        - shuffler.js
      stylesheet:
        - shuffler.css
```

Options that define the type, render targets, and output of a project.

### Jira Format Configuration

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/reference/formats/wiki/jira.llms

Configuration options for the Jira Wiki output format in Quarto.

```APIDOC
## Jira Wiki Format Configuration

### Description
Configure Quarto documents to render as Jira Wiki markup by setting the format to 'jira'.

### Configuration Options
- **title** (string) - Document title
- **date** (string) - Document date
- **date-format** (string) - Date format for the document
- **author** (string) - Author or authors of the document
- **order** (integer) - Order for document when included in a website automatic sidebar menu
- **number-sections** (boolean) - Number section headings. Default is false.
- **shift-heading-level-by** (integer) - Shift heading levels by a positive or negative integer.
- **code-annotations** (boolean) - Set to false to hide code annotations.

### Execution Options
- **execute** (object) - Container for execution settings like `echo` and `warning`.

### Rendering Options
- **from** (string) - Format to read from.
- **output-file** (string) - Output file to write to.
- **output-ext** (string) - Extension to use for generated output file.
- **template** (string) - Custom template file for the generated document.
- **filters** (list) - Executables or Lua scripts to transform the pandoc AST.
- **keep-md** (boolean) - Keep the markdown file generated by executing code.
- **dpi** (integer) - Default dpi value for conversion. Default is 96.
```

### Quarto Preview Command

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/cli/preview.llms

The `quarto preview` command is used to render and preview a document or website project. It automatically reloads the browser when input files or resources change. For website previews, it uses the most recent execution results for optimization. You can also pass arbitrary command-line arguments to `quarto render`.

```APIDOC
## quarto preview

### Description
Render and preview a document or website project. Automatically reloads the browser when input files or document resources (e.g. CSS) change.

### Method
CLI Command

### Endpoint
N/A (CLI Command)

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
- **file** (string) - Optional - The document file to preview (e.g., `doc.qmd`). If not specified, it previews the project.

#### Query Parameters
N/A

#### Request Body
N/A

### Options
| Flags | Arguments | Description |
|:---|:---|:---|
| `-h`, `--help` |  | Show this help. |
| `--port` | `[port:number]` | Suggested port to listen on (defaults to random value between 3000 and 8000). If the port is not available then a random port between 3000 and 8000 will be selected. |
| `--host` | `[host:string]` | Hostname to bind to (defaults to 127.0.0.1) |
| `--render` | `[format:string]` | Render to the specified format(s) before previewing |
| `--no-serve` |  | Don't run a local preview web server (just monitor and re-render input files) |
| `--no-navigate` |  | Don't navigate the browser automatically when outputs are updated. |
| `--no-browser` |  | Don't open a browser to preview the site. |
| `--no-watch-inputs` |  | Do not re-render input files when they change. |
| `--timeout` |  | Time (in seconds) after which to exit if there are no active clients. |
| `--log` | `[path:string]` | Path to log file |
| `--log-level` | `[level:string]` | Log level (debug, info, warning, error, critical) |
| `--log-format` | `[format:string]` | Log format (plain, json-stream) |
| `--quiet` |  | Suppress console output. |
| `--profile` | `[profile:string]` | Active project profile(s) |

### Commands
| Command | Description |
|:---|:---|
| `help`  | Show this help or the help of a sub-command. |

### Examples
#### Preview document
```bash
quarto preview doc.qmd
```

#### Preview document with render command line args
```bash
quarto preview doc.qmd --toc
```

#### Preview document (don’t watch for input changes)
```bash
quarto preview doc.qmd --no-watch-inputs
```

#### Preview website with most recent execution results
```bash
quarto preview
```

#### Previewing website using a specific port
```bash
quarto preview --port 4444
```

#### Preview website (don’t open a browser)
```bash
quarto preview --no-browser
```

#### Fully render all website/book formats then preview
```bash
quarto preview --render all
```

#### Fully render the html format then preview
```bash
quarto preview --render html
```
```

--------------------------------

### Render Current Project

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/cli/render.llms

Render all documents within the current project directory. This command assumes you are in the project's root directory.

```bash
quarto render
```

--------------------------------

### Quarto Pub Configuration (_publish.yml)

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/publishing/quarto-pub.llms

This YAML file specifies the publishing destination for Quarto Pub. It includes the service, an ID, and the URL of the published content. It's suitable for version control as it doesn't store account information.

```yaml
- source: project
  quarto-pub:
    - id: "5f3abafe-68f9-4c1d-835b-9d668b892001"
      url: "https://njones.quarto.pub/blog"
```

--------------------------------

### Extension Configuration

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/extensions/shortcodes.llms

The YAML configuration file for the shortcode extension.

```yaml
title: Shorty
author: J.J. Allaire
version: 1.0.0
quarto-required: ">=1.2.222"
contributes:
  shortcodes:
    - shorty.lua
```

--------------------------------

### Set XWiki Format

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/reference/formats/wiki/xwiki.llms

Specify the output format as XWiki. This is typically set in the document's YAML metadata.

```yaml
format: xwiki
```

--------------------------------

### Delegate Syntax Highlighting to Native System

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/output-formats/typst.llms

Use `syntax-highlighting: idiomatic` to delegate code highlighting to the output format's native system instead of Pandoc's Skylighting engine. This is the default for Typst output since Quarto 1.9.

```yaml
syntax-highlighting: idiomatic
```

Renders a specific document or an entire project directory.

```r
library(quarto)
quarto_render("document.qmd")
```

```r
library(quarto)
quarto_render()
```

library(quarto)
quarto_serve("document.qmd")
```

### Configure Dev Container for Quarto

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/blog/posts/2025-05-19-quarto-codespaces/index.llms

Defines the build environment, required computing dependencies, and VS Code customizations for a Quarto-ready Codespace.

```json
{
  "name": "Quarto",
  // "image": "buildpack-deps:jammy-curl", // <1>
  "build": {
    "dockerfile": "./Dockerfile",
    "context": ".",
    "args": {
      "VARIANT": "jammy"
    }
  },
  "remoteUser": "vscode",
  "features": { // <2>
    "./quarto-computing-dependencies": { // <3>
      "rDeps": "rmarkdown,languageserver,nx10/httpgd@v2.0.3,prompt,lintr",
      "pythonDeps": "jupyter,papermill",
      "juliaDeps": "IJulia"
    },
    "./uv": { // <4>
      "version": "latest"
    },
    "ghcr.io/rocker-org/devcontainer-features/quarto-cli:1": { // <5>
      "version": "release",
      "installTinyTex": "true",
      "installChromium": "false"
    }
  },
  "customizations": { // <6>
    "vscode": {
      "extensions": [
        "quarto.quarto",
        "mcanouil.quarto-wizard",
        "REditorSupport.r",
        "Posit.air-vscode"
      ],
      "settings": {
        "r.rterm.option": [
          "--no-save",
          "--no-restore-data",
          "--quiet"
        ],
        "[r]": {
          "editor.defaultFormatter": "Posit.air-vscode",
          "editor.formatOnSave": true
        }
      }
    }
  }
}
```

```

--------------------------------

### GitHub Action for Jupyter with venv

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/publishing/rstudio-connect.llms

This GitHub Action sets up Python, Jupyter, and package dependencies from requirements.txt, then renders and publishes the Quarto project to Connect.

```yaml
on:
  workflow_dispatch:
  push:
    branches: main

name: Quarto Publish

jobs:
  build-deploy:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Check out repository
        uses: actions/checkout@v4 

      - name: Set up Quarto
        uses: quarto-dev/quarto-actions/setup@v2
        
      - name: Install Python and Dependencies
        uses: actions/setup-python@v5
        with:
          python-version: '3.10'
          cache: 'pip'
      - run: pip install jupyter
      - run: pip install -r requirements.txt
      
      - name: Render and Publish 
        uses: quarto-dev/quarto-actions/publish@v2
        with:
          target: connect
          CONNECT_SERVER: https://connect.example.com
          CONNECT_API_KEY: ${{ secrets.CONNECT_API_KEY }}
```

--------------------------------

### Adapting Output Based on Figure Settings in Python

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/advanced/quarto-execute-info.llms

Use execution settings for figure dimensions and DPI to adapt visualization parameters. Requires the 'QUARTO_EXECUTE_INFO' environment variable.

```python
import os
import json
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

with open(os.environ["QUARTO_EXECUTE_INFO"]) as f:
    info = json.load(f)

fig_width = info["format"]["execute"]["fig-width"]
fig_height = info["format"]["execute"]["fig-height"]
fig_dpi = info["format"]["execute"]["fig-dpi"]

plt.figure(figsize=(fig_width, fig_height), dpi=fig_dpi)
plt.plot(x, y)
plt.show()
```

### Configure Latexmk Engine Options

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/output-formats/pdf-engine.llms

Use pdf-engine-opts to pass specific arguments to the PDF engine when latex-auto-mk is disabled.

```yaml
latex-auto-mk: false
pdf-engine: latexmk
pdf-engine-opts:
  - '-auxdir=custom-aux'
  - '-emulate-aux-dir'
```

### Implement Cross-Version Import Strategy

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/projects/scripts.llms

Use a dynamic import wrapper to attempt loading modules from multiple sources, ensuring compatibility between Quarto 1.5 and 1.6.

```typescript
const multiImport = async (...sources: string[]) => {
    for (const source of sources) {
        try {
            return await import(source);
        } catch (e) {}
    }
}
const { readLines } = await multiImport(
  "stdlib/io", // Quarto 1.6 syntax
  "https://deno.land/std/io/mod.ts", // Quarto 1.5 syntax
);
```

You may want to try searching to find the page's new location.

import { chart } with { pdata as data } from "@d3/zoomable-sunburst"
chart

### Render Quarto Document Using CLI Flag Behavior

To replicate the old CLI flag behavior for output files, use the `quarto_args` parameter with `quarto_render`. This allows direct use of command-line arguments.

```r
# Use CLI flag directly
quarto_render("doc.qmd", quarto_args = c("--output", "report.html"))
```

### Hugo Project Detection and Preview

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/extensions/project-types.llms

Details the project detection, rendering, and preview settings for a Hugo project type. The `detect` option specifies files to activate the type, `render` lists files to process, and `preview` configures the Hugo server launch.

```yaml
project:
  type: default
  detect:
    - ["config.toml", "content"]
    - ["config/_default/config.toml", "content"]
  render:
    - "**/*.qmd"
    - "**/*.ipynb"
  preview:
    serve:
      cmd: "hugo serve --port {port} --bind {host} --navigateToChanged"
      env: 
        HUGO_RELATIVEURLS: "true"
      ready: "Web Server is available at"

```

--------------------------------

### Implement git-rev shortcode with metadata

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/extensions/shortcodes.llms

Uses document metadata to generate a GitHub repository link from a git revision.

```lua
function git(command)
  local p = io.popen("git " .. command)
  local output = p:read('*all')
  p:close()
  return output
end

return {
  
  ["git-rev"] = function(args, kwargs, meta)
    -- run the command
    local rev = git("rev-parse HEAD")
    
    -- target repo
    local owner = pandoc.utils.stringify(meta["github.owner"])
    local repo = pandoc.utils.stringify(meta["github.repo"])
    local url = "https://github.com/" 
                .. owner .. "/" .. repo .. "/" .. rev 
    
    -- return as link
    return pandoc.Link(pandoc.Str(rev), url)
  end
}
```

### Quarto Publish GitHub Action Workflow

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/publishing/quarto-pub.llms

This YAML file defines a GitHub Actions workflow for rendering and publishing Quarto projects. It checks out the repository, sets up Quarto, and uses the `quarto-actions/publish` action.

```yaml
on:
  workflow_dispatch:
  push:
    branches: main

name: Quarto Publish

jobs:
  build-deploy:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Check out repository
        uses: actions/checkout@v4 

      - name: Set up Quarto
        uses: quarto-dev/quarto-actions/setup@v2

      - name: Render and Publish 
        uses: quarto-dev/quarto-actions/publish@v2
        with:
          target: quarto-pub
          QUARTO_PUB_AUTH_TOKEN: ${{ secrets.QUARTO_PUB_AUTH_TOKEN }}
```

### Implement Shortcode with Named Arguments

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/extensions/shortcodes.llms

A Lua implementation using a returned table to define shortcodes and handle named arguments via kwargs.

```lua
-- run git and read its output
function git(command)
  local p = io.popen("git " .. command)
  local output = p:read('*all')
  p:close()
  return output
end

-- return a table containing shortcode definitions
-- defining shortcodes this way allows us to create helper 
-- functions that are not themselves considered shortcodes 
return {
  ["git-rev"] = function(args, kwargs)
    -- command line args
    local cmdArgs = ""
    local short = pandoc.utils.stringify(kwargs["short"])
    if short == "true" then
      cmdArgs = cmdArgs .. "--short "
    end
    
    -- run the command
    local cmd = "rev-parse " .. cmdArgs .. "HEAD"
    local rev = git(cmd)
    
    -- return as string
    return pandoc.Str(rev)
  end
}
```

### Quarto CLI Commands

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/cli/index.llms

Overview of available Quarto CLI commands for project lifecycle management.

```APIDOC
## CLI Commands

### Description
Use the Quarto CLI to interact with Quarto from the terminal. Append `--help` to any command to view specific options.

### Commands
- **render** - Render files or projects to various document types.
- **preview** - Render and preview a document or website project.
- **serve** - Serve a Shiny interactive document.
- **create** - Create a Quarto project or extension.
- **use** - Automate document or project setup tasks.
- **add** - Add an extension to this folder or project.
- **update** - Updates an extension or global dependency.
- **remove** - Removes an extension.
- **convert** - Convert documents to alternate representations.
- **pandoc** - Run the version of Pandoc embedded within Quarto.
- **typst** - Run the version of Typst embedded within Quarto.
- **run** - Run a TypeScript, R, Python, or Lua script.
- **list** - Lists an extension or global dependency.
- **install** - Installs a global dependency.
- **uninstall** - Uninstalls a global dependency.
- **tools** - Display the status of Quarto installed dependencies.
- **publish** - Publish a document or project to a provider.
- **capabilities** - Query for current capabilities.
- **inspect** - Inspect a Quarto project or input path.
- **check** - Verify correct functioning of Quarto installation.
- **call** - Access functions of Quarto subsystems.

### Usage Example
```bash
quarto render document.qmd
quarto render --help
```
```

### quarto.Callout Constructor

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/prerelease/1.3/custom-ast-nodes/callout.llms

API reference for creating callout AST nodes in Lua filters.

```APIDOC
## quarto.Callout Constructor

### Description
Creates a new callout AST node for use in Quarto Lua filters.

### Parameters
#### Request Body
- **type** (string) - Optional - The type of callout (e.g., 'note', 'caution', 'warning').
- **title** (string) - Optional - The title of the callout.
- **icon** (boolean|string) - Optional - The callout icon or false if none.
- **appearance** (string) - Optional - The visual style: 'minimal', 'simple', or 'default'.
- **collapse** (boolean) - Optional - Whether the callout is collapsible (default: false).
- **content** (pandoc.Blocks|list) - Required - The content of the callout.

### Request Example
{
  "type": "note",
  "title": "My Title",
  "content": [pandoc.Para("Hello World")]
}
```

### Define extension metadata

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/extensions/brand.llms

The _extension.yml file defines the extension's metadata and links the brand configuration.

```yaml
title: My-brand
author: Gordon Woodhull
version: 1.0.0
quarto-required: ">=99.9.0"
contributes:
  metadata:
    project:
      brand: brand.yml
```

### Publishing to Confluence

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/publishing/ci.llms

Render and publish to Confluence using authentication and domain credentials.

```bash
# render and publish to Confluence based on _publish.yml
export CONFLUENCE_AUTH_TOKEN=7C0947A852D8
export CONFLUENCE_USER_EMAIL=email@domain.com
export CONFLUENCE_DOMAIN=https://domain.atlassian.net/
quarto publish confluence --no-browser --no-prompt
```

### Multiple Output Formats with Options

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/get-started/authoring/jupyter.llms

Specify multiple output formats (HTML, PDF, DOCX) with format-specific options. Options like 'toc' and 'number-sections' at the root level apply to all formats.

```yaml
---
title: "Quarto Document"
author: "Norah Jones"
toc: true
number-sections: true
syntax-highlighting: pygments
format: 
  html: 
    code-fold: true
    html-math-method: katex
  pdf: 
    geometry: 
      - top=30mm
      - left=20mm
  docx: default
jupyter: python3
---
```

### Update Deno Standard Library Imports

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/projects/scripts.llms

Use the 'stdlib/' prefix for standard library imports in Quarto 1.6, replacing the previous remote URL syntax.

```typescript
import { parse } from "stdlib/yaml"; // Quarto 1.6 syntax
import { parse } from "https://deno.land/std/yaml/mod.ts"; // Quarto 1.5 and earlier syntax

const config = parse(Deno.readTextFileSync("_quarto.yml"));
```

### Control Caching via Command Line

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/computations/julia.llms

Use Quarto render flags to override caching behavior for specific execution runs.

```bash
# use a cache (even if not enabled in options)
quarto render example.qmd --cache 

# don't use a cache (even if enabled in options)
quarto render example.qmd --no-cache 

# use a cache and force a refresh 
quarto render example.qmd --cache-refresh
```

### Basic Shiny Dashboard Structure

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/dashboards/interactivity/shiny-python/index.llms

This is the foundational structure for a Shiny-enabled Quarto dashboard. It includes front matter to enable the Shiny server and imports necessary libraries.

```yaml
---
title: "Penguin Bills"
format: dashboard
server: shiny # <1>
---

```{{python}}
import seaborn as sns
penguins = sns.load_dataset("penguins")
```

## {.sidebar} # <2>

```{{python}}
from shiny.express import render, ui
ui.input_select("x", "Variable:",   # <3>
                choices=["bill_length_mm", "bill_depth_mm"])
ui.input_select("dist", "Distribution:", choices=["hist", "kde"])
ui.input_checkbox("rug", "Show rug marks", value = False)  # <3>
```

## Column

```{{python}}
@render.plot # <4>
def displot():
    sns.displot(
        data=penguins, hue="species", multiple="stack",
        x=input.x(), rug=input.rug(), kind=input.dist()) # <4>
```
```

### Create Heatmap Tables with R and Python

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/output-formats/typst.llms

Use gt in R or pandas in Python to generate tables that translate CSS styles to Typst.

```r
```{r}
library(gt)
temps <- data.frame(
  year = c(1920:1924),
  Jan = c(40.6, 44.2, 37.5, 41.8, 39.3), 
  Jun = c(58.5, 58.7, 57.8, 52.7, 57.7)
)
temps |>
  gt() |> 
  data_color(
    columns = c(-year),
    fn = scales::col_numeric(
      colorspace::diverge_hcl(n = 9,
        palette = "Green-Orange"),
      domain = c(35, 62))
  )

```
```

```python
```{python}
import pandas as pd
import numpy as np

temps = pd.DataFrame({
  'year': [*range(1920, 1925)],
  'Jan': [40.6, 44.2, 37.5, 41.8, 39.3], 
  'Jun': [58.5, 58.7, 57.8, 52.7, 57.7]
}).set_index('year')

def make_pretty(styler):
  styler.background_gradient(axis=None,
    vmin=31, vmax=66, cmap="RdYlGn_r")
  return styler

temps.style.pipe(make_pretty)

```
```

### Julia Plots Demo

title: "Plots Demo"

    code-fold: true

---

## Parametric Plots

Plot function pair (x(u), y(u)). 
See @fig-parametric for an example.

```{julia}
#| label: fig-parametric
#| fig-cap: "Parametric Plots"

using Plots

plot(sin, 
     x->sin(2x), 
     0, 
     2π, 
     leg=false, 
     fill=(0,:lavender))
```

--------------------------------

### Configure Navbar in _quarto.yml

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/websites/website-navigation.llms

Defines the structure and appearance of the website navigation bar.

```APIDOC
## Configuration: website.navbar

### Description
Configures the top navigation bar for a Quarto website. This is defined within the `website` section of the `_quarto.yml` file.

### Configuration Options
- **title** (string) - Navbar title; defaults to site title. Use `false` to suppress.
- **logo** (string) - Path to logo image. Use `false` to suppress.
- **logo-alt** (string) - Alternate text for the logo.
- **logo-href** (string) - Target URL for the logo/title.
- **background** (string) - Background color (e.g., "primary", "dark", or hex).
- **foreground** (string) - Foreground color for text and links.
- **search** (boolean) - Enable or disable the search box.
- **left** / **right** (list) - Lists of navigation items for the respective sides.
- **pinned** (boolean) - If true, always show the navbar.
- **collapse** (boolean) - Collapse items into a hamburger menu on small screens.

### Navigation Item Options
- **href** (string) - Link to a file or external URL.
- **text** (string) - Display text for the item.
- **icon** (string) - Bootstrap 5 icon name.
- **menu** (list) - List of items to create a drop-down menu.

### Example Configuration
```yaml
website:
  navbar:
    background: primary
    search: true
    left:
      - text: "Home"
        href: index.qmd
      - text: "More"
        menu:
          - talks.qmd
          - about.qmd
```
```

### Accessing Execution Information in Python

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/advanced/quarto-execute-info.llms

Demonstrates how to read the QUARTO_EXECUTE_INFO environment variable and parse the JSON file to access document path and format details.

```APIDOC
## Accessing Execution Information in Python

### Description
This snippet shows how to access Quarto's execution context information within a Python environment. It reads the `QUARTO_EXECUTE_INFO` environment variable to locate a JSON file containing metadata about the current document rendering process.

### Method
Environment Variable Access and File I/O

### Endpoint
N/A (Environment Variable)

### Parameters
#### Environment Variables
- **QUARTO_EXECUTE_INFO** (string) - Required - Path to the JSON file containing execution metadata.

### Request Example
```python
import os
import json

with open(os.environ["QUARTO_EXECUTE_INFO"]) as f:
    info = json.load(f)

# Access document path
print(info["document-path"])

# Access format information
print(info["format"]["identifier"]["target-format"])
```

### Response
#### Success Response (stdout)
- **document-path** (string) - The absolute path to the source document being rendered.
- **target-format** (string) - The target output format identifier (e.g., “gfm”, “html”).

#### Response Example
```
/path/to/your/document.qmd
github
```
```

### CLI: quarto render

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/cli/render.llms

The render command processes input files or projects and generates output documents based on specified formats and configuration options.

```APIDOC
## CLI Command: quarto render

### Description
Render files or projects to various document types.

### Usage
`quarto render [input:string] [...args]`

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
- **input** (string) - Optional - The path to the file or project directory to render.

#### Options
- **-h, --help** - Show help.
- **-t, --to** - Specify output format(s).
- **-o, --output** - Write output to FILE (use '--output -' for stdout).
- **--output-dir** - Write output to DIR (path is input/project relative).
- **-M, --metadata** - Metadata value (KEY:VALUE).
- **--site-url** - Override site-url for website or book output.
- **--execute** - Execute code (--no-execute to skip execution).
- **-P, --execute-param** - Execution parameter (KEY:VALUE).
- **--execute-params** - YAML file with execution parameters.
- **--execute-dir** - Working directory for code execution.
- **--execute-daemon** - Keep Jupyter kernel alive (defaults to 300 seconds).
- **--execute-daemon-restart** - Restart keepalive Jupyter kernel before render.
- **--execute-debug** - Show debug output when executing computations.
- **--use-freezer** - Force use of frozen computations for an incremental file render.
- **--cache** - Cache execution output (--no-cache to prevent cache).
- **--cache-refresh** - Force refresh of execution cache.
- **--no-clean** - Do not clean project output-dir prior to render.
- **--debug** - Leave intermediate files in place after render.
- **pandoc-args...** - Additional pandoc command line arguments.
- **--log** - Path to log file.
- **--log-level** - Log level (debug, info, warning, error, critical).
- **--log-format** - Log format (plain, json-stream).
- **--quiet** - Suppress console output.
- **--profile** - Active project profile(s).

### Examples
- Render Markdown: `quarto render document.qmd --to html`
- Render Notebook: `quarto render notebook.ipynb --to pdf --toc`
- Render Project: `quarto render projdir`
- Render to Stdout: `quarto render document.qmd --output -`
```

--------------------------------

### Implement Tabsets in Markdown

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/output-formats/html-basics.llms

Use the panel-tabset class to create tabbed content blocks.

```markdown
::: {.panel-tabset}
## R

``` {.r}
fizz_buzz <- function(fbnums = 1:50) {
  output <- dplyr::case_when(
    fbnums %% 15 == 0 ~ "FizzBuzz",
    fbnums %% 3 == 0 ~ "Fizz",
    fbnums %% 5 == 0 ~ "Buzz",
    TRUE ~ as.character(fbnums)
  )
  print(output)
}
```

## Python

``` {.python}
def fizz_buzz(num):
  if num % 15 == 0:
    print("FizzBuzz")
  elif num % 5 == 0:
    print("Buzz")
  elif num % 3 == 0:
    print("Fizz")
  else:
    print(num)
```

:::
```

```markdown
::: {.panel-tabset group="language"}
## R

Tab content

## Python

Tab content
:::
```

```markdown
::: {.panel-tabset}
## R

Tab content

## Python {.active}

Tab content
:::
```

--------------------------------

### Quarto Custom Node Constructors

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/advanced/quarto-ast.llms

Details on using Quarto's constructors for creating custom AST nodes in Lua filters.

```APIDOC
## Quarto Custom AST Node Constructors

### Description
Quarto provides constructors within the `quarto` object to create custom AST nodes in Lua filters. These include `quarto.Callout`, `quarto.Tabset`, `quarto.Tab`, and `quarto.ConditionalBlock`.

### Callout Constructor
`quarto.Callout(options)`

- **options** (table) - A table with the following optional entries:
  - `type` (string): The type of callout (e.g., `note`, `caution`, `warning`).
  - `title` (pandoc.Inlines): The callout title.
  - `icon` (pandoc.Inlines | boolean): The callout icon or `false`.
  - `appearance` (string): The appearance style (`"minimal"`, `"simple"`, or `"default"`).
  - `collapse` (boolean): Whether the callout should be collapsible (default `false`).
  - `content` (pandoc.Blocks | list): The content of the callout.

### Tabset Constructor
`quarto.Tabset(options)`

- **options** (table) - A table with the following optional entries:
  - `tabs` (list): A list of tab objects, each with `title` (pandoc.Inlines) and `content` (pandoc.Blocks).
  - `level` (integer): The heading level for tab headings (default `2`).
  - `attr` (pandoc.Attr): The `Attr` object for the tabset div.

### Tab Constructor
`quarto.Tab(options)`

- **options** (table) - A table with the following entries:
  - `title` (pandoc.Inlines): The tab title.
  - `content` (pandoc.Blocks): The tab content.

### ConditionalBlock Constructor
`quarto.ConditionalBlock(options)`

- **options** (table) - A table with the following entries:
  - `node` (pandoc.Div): The div containing the content.
  - `behavior` (string): Either `"content-visible"` or `"content-hidden"`.
  - `condition` (list): A list of conditions, e.g., `{ { "unless-format", "html" } }`. Each sublist has a key (`when-format`, `unless-format`, `when-profile`, `unless-profile`) and a value (format or profile name).
```

### Implement Revealjs Plugin Logic

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/extensions/revealjs.llms

JavaScript implementation for the RevealAttribution plugin, handling slide initialization and dynamic resizing.

```javascript
window.RevealAttribution = window.RevealAttribution || {
  id: 'RevealAttribution',
  init: function(deck) {
      initAttribution(deck);
  }
};

const initAttribution = function(Reveal){

var ready = false;
var resize = false;
var scale = 1;

window.addEventListener( 'ready', function( event ) {

  var content;

  // Remove configured margin of the presentation
  var attribution = document.getElementsByClassName("attribution");
  var width = window.innerWidth;
  var configuredWidth = Reveal.getConfig().width;
  var configuredHeight = Reveal.getConfig().height;

  scale = 1/(1-Reveal.getConfig().margin);

  for (var i = 0; i < attribution.length; i++) {
    content = attribution[i].innerHTML;
    attribution[i].style.width = configuredWidth + "px";
    attribution[i].style.height = configuredHeight + "px";
    attribution[i].innerHTML = "<span class='content'>" + content + "</span>";
    attribution[i].style.transform = 'translate( -50%, -50% ) scale( ' + scale*100 + '% ) rotate(-180deg)';
  }

  // Scale with cover class to mimic backgroundSize cover
  resizeCover();

});

window.addEventListener( 'resize', resizeCover );

function resizeCover() {

  // Scale to mimic backgroundSize cover
  var attribution = document.getElementsByClassName("attribution");
  var xScale = window.innerWidth / Reveal.getConfig().width;
  var yScale = window.innerHeight / Reveal.getConfig().height;
  var s = 1;

  if (xScale > yScale) {
      // The div fits perfectly in x axis, stretched in y
      s = xScale/yScale;
  }
  for (var i = 0; i < attribution.length; i++) {
    attribution[i].style.transform = 'translate( -50%, -50% ) scale( ' + s*scale*100 + '% ) rotate(-180deg)';
  }
}

};
```

### DocBook Configuration Options

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/reference/formats/docbook.llms

Configuration options for DocBook format, including metadata, execution, and rendering settings.

```APIDOC
## DocBook Configuration

### Description
Defines the configuration schema for DocBook output in Quarto.

### Format Options
- **format** (string) - Required - Set to 'docbook'.

### Title & Author
- **title** (string) - Document title
- **date** (string) - Document date
- **date-format** (string) - Date format for the document
- **author** (string) - Author or authors of the document
- **order** (integer) - Order for document when included in a website automatic sidebar menu.

### Execution
- **execute** (object) - Execution options
  - **echo** (boolean) - Whether to echo code
  - **warning** (boolean) - Whether to show warnings

### Rendering
- **from** (string) - Format to read from
- **output-file** (string) - Output file to write to
- **output-ext** (string) - Extension to use for generated output file
- **template** (string) - Custom template file
- **filters** (list) - Executables or Lua scripts for AST transformation
- **keep-md** (boolean) - Keep generated markdown file
- **dpi** (integer) - Default dpi value (default: 96)
```

--------------------------------

--------------------------------

### Create D3 Hierarchy and Partition Layout

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/interactive/ojs/libraries.llms

Prepare hierarchical data for D3.js visualizations by creating a hierarchy, summing values, and applying a partition layout. Requires D3 to be imported.

```javascript
partition = flareData => {
  const root = d3.hierarchy(flareData)
      .sum(d => d.value)
      .sort((a, b) => b.value - a.value);
  return d3.partition()
      .size([2 * Math.PI, root.height + 1])
    (root);
}
```

### quarto use brand

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/cli/use.llms

Use a specific brand for the current project.

```APIDOC
## quarto use brand

### Description
Use a brand for this project.

### Method
CLI Command

### Endpoint
quarto use brand <target:string>

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
- **target** (string) - Required - The brand to use, often specified as a GitHub repository (e.g., <gh-org>/<gh-repo>).

#### Query Parameters
None

#### Request Body
None

### Options
#### Flags
- **--force** - Skip all prompts and confirmations
- **--dry-run** - Show what would happen without making changes
- **--log** (Path to log file)
- **--log-level** (Log level: debug, info, warning, error, critical)
- **--log-format** (Log format: plain, json-stream)
- **--quiet** - Suppress console output.
- **--profile** (Active project profile(s))

### Examples
#### Use a brand from Github
```bash
quarto use brand <gh-org>/<gh-repo>
```
```

### Control Caching with Quarto Render CLI

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/computations/python.llms

Use command-line options with `quarto render` to control caching behavior without modifying document options. Options include forcing cache usage, disabling cache, or forcing a cache refresh.

```bash
quarto render example.qmd --cache 
# use a cache (even if not enabled in options)
```

```bash
quarto render example.qmd --no-cache 
# don't use a cache (even if enabled in options)
```

```bash
quarto render example.qmd --cache-refresh 
# use a cache and force a refresh
```

### Configure Dev Container with Docker Image

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/blog/posts/2025-05-19-quarto-codespaces/index.llms

```json
{
  "name": "My Workshop Setup",
  "image": "ghcr.io/mcanouil/quarto-codespaces:latest",
  "remoteUser": "vscode",
  "customizations": {
    "vscode": {
      "extensions": [
        "quarto.quarto",
        "mcanouil.quarto-wizard"
      ]
    },
    "codespaces": {
      "openFiles": [
        "exercises/intro-to-quarto.qmd",
        "exercises/computation.qmd"
      ]
    }
  }
}
```

### Create Cross-Referenceable Table with Python

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/authoring/tables.llms

Use a label with a `tbl-` prefix in executable code cells to make tables cross-referenceable. Ensure the label is set using `#| label:` and the caption with `#| tbl-cap:`.

```python
#| label: tbl-planets
#| tbl-cap: Astronomical object

from IPython.display import Markdown
from tabulate import tabulate
table = [["Sun","696,000",1.989e30],
         ["Earth","6,371",5.972e24],
         ["Moon","1,737",7.34e22],
         ["Mars","3,390",6.39e23]]
Markdown(tabulate(
  table, 
  headers=["Astronomical object","R (km)", "mass (kg)"]
))
```

### CLI: call build-ts-extension

Builds and bundles TypeScript execution engine extensions.

```APIDOC
## CLI: call build-ts-extension

### Description
Build TypeScript execution engine extensions. This command type-checks and bundles TypeScript extensions into single JavaScript files.

### Method
CLI Command

### Endpoint
quarto call build-ts-extension [entry-point:string]

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
- **entry-point** (string) - Optional - The entry point file for the extension

#### Query Parameters
- **--check** (boolean) - Optional - Type-check only (skip bundling)
- **--init-config** (boolean) - Optional - Generate deno.json with absolute importMap path
- **--log** (string) - Optional - Path to log file
- **--log-level** (string) - Optional - Log level (debug, info, warning, error, critical)
- **--log-format** (string) - Optional - Log format (plain, json-stream)
- **--quiet** (boolean) - Optional - Suppress console output

### Website Search Configuration

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/reference/projects/websites.llms

Configure website search options including location, type, and advanced settings like Algolia integration.

```APIDOC
## Website Search Configuration

### Description
Configure website search options including location, type, and advanced settings like Algolia integration.

### Parameters
#### YAML Configuration
- **website.search.location** (string) - Optional - Location for search widget (`navbar` or `sidebar`)
- **website.search.type** (string) - Optional - Type of search UI (`overlay` or `textbox`)
- **website.search.limit** (integer) - Optional - Number of matches to display (defaults to 20)
- **website.search.collapse-after** (integer) - Optional - Matches after which to collapse additional results
- **website.search.copy-button** (boolean) - Optional - Provide button for copying search link
- **website.search.merge-navbar-crumbs** (boolean) - Optional - When false, do not merge navbar crumbs into the crumbs in `search.json`.
- **website.search.keyboard-shortcut** (string or array of strings) - Optional - One or more keys that will act as a shortcut to launch search (single characters)
- **website.search.show-item-context** (boolean) - Optional - Whether to include search result parents when displaying items in search results (when possible).

### Algolia Options
Configure Algolia integration for site search.

#### YAML Configuration
- **website.search.algolia.index-name** (string) - Required - The name of the index to use when performing a search
- **website.search.algolia.application-id** (string) - Required - The unique ID used by Algolia to identify your application
- **website.search.algolia.search-only-api-key** (string) - Required - The Search-Only API key to use to connect to Algolia
- **website.search.algolia.analytics-events** (boolean) - Optional - Enable tracking of Algolia analytics events
- **website.search.algolia.show-logo** (boolean) - Optional - Enable the display of the Algolia logo in the search results footer.
- **website.search.algolia.index-fields** (object) - Optional - Fields to target for searches. Example: `{"href": "url", "title": "title", "text": "content", "section": "section"}`
- **website.search.algolia.params** (object) - Optional - Additional parameters to pass when executing a search

### Request Example
```yaml
website:
  search:
    location: navbar
    type: overlay
    limit: 30
    algolia:
      index-name: "my-index-name"
      application-id: "my-application-id"
      search-only-api-key: "my-search-only-api-key"
```
```

### Configure Quarto Document for Confluence

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/publishing/confluence.llms

Set the output format to confluence-html in the document YAML header to enable publishing to Confluence.

```markdown
---
title: Confluence Demo
format: confluence-html
---
```

--------------------------------

### Extension Configuration Schema

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/extensions/distributing.llms

Details on the structure and fields required within the _extension.yml file to define a Quarto extension.

```APIDOC
## _extension.yml Configuration

### Description
The _extension.yml file defines metadata and contributions for a Quarto extension.

### Fields
- **title** (string) - The extension name.
- **author** (string) - The author of the extension.
- **version** (string) - Semantic version number (e.g., 1.0.0).
- **quarto-required** (string) - Minimum Quarto version required.
- **contributes** (object) - Items contributed by the extension:
  - **shortcodes** (list) - List of shortcode files.
  - **filters** (list) - List of filter files.
  - **formats** (record) - Output formats and associated metadata.
  - **project** (object) - Custom project type info.
  - **revealjs-plugins** (object) - RevealJS plugin info.
  - **metadata** (object) - Metadata to be merged.
  - **brand** (object) - Brand extension info.
  - **engine** (object) - Custom engine info.

### Example
```yaml
title: My Filter
author: Cooltools
version: 1.0.0
quarto-required: ">=1.2.0"
contributes:
  filters:
    - my-filter.lua
```
```

--------------------------------

### Reference site-absolute image paths

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/websites/website-tools.llms

Use site-absolute paths for global images to ensure they are correctly converted to relative paths during publishing.

```markdown
![](/images/logo.png)
```

### Implement Cross-References

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/get-started/authoring/text-editor.llms

Assign labels to figures and equations to enable navigation and automatic numbering.

```markdown
---
title: Quarto Crossrefs
format: html
jupyter: python3
---

## Overview

See @fig-simple in @sec-plot for a demonstration of a simple plot. 

See @eq-stddev to better understand standard deviation.

## Plot {#sec-plot}

```{python}
#| label: fig-simple
#| fig-cap: "Simple Plot"
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
plt.plot([1,23,2,4])
plt.show()
```

## Equation {#sec-equation}

$$
s = \sqrt{\frac{1}{N-1} \sum_{i=1}^N (x_i - \overline{x})^2}
$$ {#eq-stddev}
```

--------------------------------

### Set Explicit Video Width and Height

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/authoring/videos.llms

Disable responsive sizing and set a fixed `width` and `height` for videos. This is useful for precise layout control.

```default
{{< video https://youtu.be/wo9vZccmqwc width="250" height="175" >}}
```

--------------------------------

### Configure Typst Fonts

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/output-formats/typst.llms

YAML configuration for setting the main document font and additional font search paths.

```yaml
---
title: "My Document"
format: 
  typst:
    mainfont: "Agbalumo"
    font-paths: myfonts
---
```

--------------------------------

### Create a Diagram Cross-Reference

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/authoring/cross-references-divs.llms

Treat diagrams like figures by wrapping them in a div with a unique ID.

```markdown
::: {#fig-simple}

```{dot}
graph {
  A -- B
}
```

This is a simple graphviz graph
:::
```

--------------------------------

### Configure Freeze Execution Options

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/computations/caching.llms

Control re-rendering behavior during global project renders using the freeze option.

```yaml
execute:
  freeze: true  # never re-render during project render
```

```yaml
execute:
  freeze: auto  # re-render only when source changes
```

--------------------------------

### Configure Global Execution Options

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/get-started/computations/jupyter.llms

Set document-wide execution behavior in the YAML header to hide code blocks.

```yaml
---
title: Quarto Computations
execute:
  echo: false
jupyter: python3
---
```

--------------------------------

### Basic Typst Document Configuration

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/output-formats/typst.llms

Use this YAML configuration to render a PDF document using Typst. It enables table of contents and custom section numbering.

```yaml
---
title: "Hello Typst!"
format:
  typst:
    toc: true
    section-numbering: 1.1.a
    columns: 2
---

```

--------------------------------

### Create multi-column layouts

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/presentations/index.llms

Use a .columns div container with nested .column divs to arrange content side-by-side.

```markdown
:::: {.columns}

::: {.column width="40%"}
contents...
:::

::: {.column width="60%"}
contents...
:::

::::
```

--------------------------------

### Enable RSS Feed for Listing

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/websites/website-listings.llms

Add the feed option to a listing configuration to generate an RSS file automatically.

```yaml
listing:
  contents: posts
  feed: true
```

### Context Format Configuration

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/reference/formats/context.llms

Specifies the document format as Context.

```APIDOC
## Format Configuration

### Description
Specifies the document format to be processed by Context.

### Method
Configuration

### Endpoint
N/A

### Request Body
```yaml
format: context
```

### Response
N/A
```

--------------------------------

### Configure Navbar Tools in YAML

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/websites/website-navigation.llms

Define navbar tools using Bootstrap icon names and hrefs within the website configuration. Supports both direct links and dropdown menus.

```yaml
website:
  navbar:
    tools:
      - icon: bluesky
        href: https://bsky.app
      - icon: github
        menu:
          - text: Source Code
            href:  https://code.com
          - text: Report a Bug
            href:  https://bugs.com
```

--------------------------------

### Request for quarto check output

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/triaging/index.llms

This markdown snippet explains how to provide the output of the `quarto check` command, which is useful for diagnosing issues. It specifies that the output should be enclosed in a `txt` code block.

```markdown
Additionally and if not already given, please share the output of `quarto check` within a code block (*i.e.*, using three backticks ` ```txt `), see <https://quarto.org/bug-reports.html#check>.
```

--------------------------------

### Use Meta Variables in Image Paths

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/blog/posts/2024-12-12-includes-meta/index.llms

Dynamically construct image paths using meta variables to maintain a single source for multiple documents.

```markdown
{{< meta state >}}'s official flower is the {{< meta flower >}}, pictured below:

![The official {{< meta state >}} state flower, the {{< meta flower >}}](../images/{{< meta state-abbr >}}/flower.png)

Lastly, {{< meta state >}}'s official animal is the {{< meta animal >}}, pictured below:

![The official {{< meta state >}} state animal, the {{< meta animal >}}](../images/{{< meta state-abbr >}}/animal.png)
```

--------------------------------

### ePub Formatting Options

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/reference/formats/epub.llms

Configuration options specifically for controlling the structure and splitting of ePub output files.

```APIDOC
## ePub Formatting

### Description
Controls the internal composition of the generated ePub file.

### Parameters
- **split-level** (integer) - Optional - Specify the heading level at which to split the EPUB into separate chapter files. Default is 1.
```

--------------------------------

### Quarto Document Reveal.js Plugin Reference

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/presentations/revealjs/advanced.llms

Add this to your document's YAML header to include the custom fullscreen plugin in your Quarto HTML presentation.

```yaml
format: 
 revealjs:
  revealjs-plugins:
    - fullscreen
```

--------------------------------

### Configure file-specific resources in YAML

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/websites/website-tools.llms

Add a resources metadata value to individual files to include specific assets.

```yaml
title: "My Page"
resources:
  - "sheet.xlsx"
```

--------------------------------

### Configure Open Graph

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/reference/projects/books.llms

Set specific Open Graph metadata options under the open-graph key.

```yaml
book:
  open-graph: 
    title: "Title for Open Graph"
```

--------------------------------

### Embed YouTube Video using Shortcode

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/authoring/markdown-basics.llms

Include videos, such as YouTube embeds, using the `{{< video >}}` shortcode. Provide the video URL as an argument to the shortcode.

```markdown
{{< video https://www.youtube.com/embed/wo9vZccmqwc >}}
```

--------------------------------

### Basic Document Metadata and Default Format

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/get-started/authoring/jupyter.llms

Define basic document metadata and set the default output format to PDF. If the 'format' option is omitted, it defaults to HTML.

```yaml
---
title: "Quarto Document"
author: "Norah Jones"
format: pdf
jupyter: python3
---
```

--------------------------------

### Navbar Configuration

Source: https://quarto.org/docs/reference/projects/books.llms

Options that define the top navigation bar for a book.

```APIDOC
## Navbar Configuration

### Description
Options that define the top navigation bar for a book.

### Parameters
#### Request Body
- **book.navbar** (object) - Optional - Navbar configuration options.
  - **title** (string) - Optional - The navbar title. Uses the project title if none is specified.
  - **logo** (string) - Optional - Specification of image that will be displayed to the left of the title.
  - **logo-alt** (string) - Optional - Alternate text for the logo image.
  - **logo-href** (string) - Optional - Target href from navbar logo / title. By default, the logo and title link to the root page of the site (/index.html).
  - **background** (string) - Optional - The navbar’s background color (named or hex color).
  - **foreground** (string) - Optional - The navbar’s foreground color (named or hex color).
  - **search** (boolean) - Optional - Include a search box in the navbar.
  - **pinned** (boolean) - Optional - Always show the navbar (keeping it pinned).
  - **collapse** (boolean) - Optional - Collapse the navbar into a menu when the display becomes narrow.
  - **collapse-below** (string) - Optional - The responsive breakpoint below which the navbar will collapse into a menu (`sm`, `md`, `lg` (default), `xl`, `xxl`).
  - **left** (array) - Optional - List of items for the left side of the navbar (see [Nav Items](#nav-items)).
  - **right** (array) - Optional - List of items for the right side of the navbar (see [Nav Items](#nav-items)).
  - **toggle-position** (string) - Optional - The position of the collapsed navbar toggle when in responsive mode.
  - **tools-collapse** (boolean) - Optional - Collapse tools into the navbar menu when the display becomes narrow.
```
